Quranic Emphasis on Knowledge
Author discusses the Quran's emphasis on knowledge using verses and statistics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Quranic evidence for the emphasis on knowledge and distinguish between the terms 'ilm and ma'rifa in Quranic usage.

Core Idea
The Quran elevates knowledge by frequency, distinction, and positioning it before creation.

The Quran repeatedly emphasizes knowledge, using specific terms and placing it even before the creation of humanity. This lesson helps you parse the Quranic evidence and the numerical data provided, so you can appreciate why knowledge is central in Islam and how to engage with the Quran accordingly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verses cited
Locate the three main verses used to show the importance of knowledge: 3:18 (Allah, angels, people of knowledge uphold justice), 58:11 (Raising of ranks for believers given knowledge), and 13:19 (knowing vs. blind). Also note the Surah Ar-Rahman verses connecting knowledge before and after creation.
Each verse adds a different dimension: justice, status, and sight/blindness.
2
Extract the frequency data
Note the numbers: the root 'alima' occurs ~850 times, 'arafa' ~71 times. The term 'ilm appears ~400 times for human knowledge; the rest for divine knowledge. 'Ma'rifa is exclusively human.
The footnotes to original sources give authority to the numbers.
3
Distinguish between 'ilm and ma'rifa
Understand that in this passage, 'ilm can refer to both divine and human knowledge, while ma'rifa is only human. This is a key terminological distinction in Quranic usage.
In later Sufi contexts, ma'rifa often takes on a more spiritual meaning.
4
Connect to the need for proper Quranic engagement
The author concludes that because the Quran emphasizes knowledge so much, we must learn how to properly engage with it – its civilizational importance demands attention to intellectual, emotional, and behavioral etiquettes.
This leads to the study of 'adab al-ilm' (etiquette of knowledge) and Quranic hermeneutics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هُوَ وَالْمَلائِكَةُ وَأُولُو الْعِلْمِ قَائِماً بِالْقِسْطِ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ الْعَزِيزُ الْحَكِيمُ آل عمران: ۱۸/۳]. وللعلماء العاملين درجات متميزة: ﴿يَرْفَعِ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنكُمْ وَالَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْعِلْمَ دَرَجَاتِ ﴾ [المجادلة: ١١/٥٨]. وفرق بين العالم والجاهل بوصف الأول عاقلاً مبصراً، والآخر جاهلاً أعمى: أَفَمَنْ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّما أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِنْ رَبِّكَ الْحَقُّ كَمَنْ هُوَ أَعْمَى إِنَّمَا يَتَذَكَّرُ أُولُو الألباب﴾ [الرعد: ١٩/١٣]. وذكر القرآن المعرفة قبل ذكر خلق الإنسان وبعده: ﴿الرَّحْمَنُ، عَلْمَ الْقُرْآنَ، خَلَقَ الإِنسانَ، عَلْمَهُ الْبَيان ﴾ [الرحمن: ١/٥٥ - ٤]. وحاصل القول هنا : أن القرآن الكريم قد اهتم بقضية العلم إلى الحد الذي جعل فعل (عَلِمَ ) ومشتقاته يتكرر في القرآن نحواً من ٨٥٠ مرة (١) ، كما تكرر فعل (عَرَف ( ومشتقاته ۷۱ مــرة (۳). ويلاحظ أن دلالة لفظ العلم وردت في حوالي ٤٠٠ موضع منها دالة على العلم الإنساني، أما ما وردت في غير تلك المواضع فدالة على علم الله عز وجل، بينما اقتصر ورود لفظ المعرفة في دلالته على العلم الإنساني فحسب (۳). ونظراً لكل هذا الاهتمام الواضح بالعلم والمعرفة في القرآن الكريم، فإن ثمة ضرورة ملحة لمعرفة كيفية التعامل مع القرآن الكريم لأهميته الحضارية في ميدان المعرفة. وقد أفرد لها بعض العلماء كتاباً شاملاً تناول المسائل ذات الصلة بهذا الجانب، على نحو يكاد يستغرق الآداب المعرفية والوجدانية والسلوكية (4) .
He, the angels, and the people of knowledge stand firmly for justice; there is no god but Him, the Mighty, the Wise [Quran 3:18]. And for the knowledgeable workers there are distinct degrees: 'Allah will raise those who have believed among you and those who were given knowledge by degrees' [Quran 58:11]. And He distinguishes between the knowledgeable and the ignorant by describing the former as rational and seeing, and the latter as ignorant and blind: 'Is he who knows that what has been revealed to you from your Lord is the truth like him who is blind? Only those of understanding will remember' [Quran 13:19]. And the Quran mentioned knowledge before and after the creation of man: 'The Most Merciful, taught the Quran, created man, taught him eloquence' [Quran 55:1-4]. The conclusion here is that the Noble Quran has concerned itself with the issue of knowledge to the extent that the verb 'alima' and its derivatives occur in the Quran about 850 times (1), and the verb 'arafa' and its derivatives occur 71 times (2). It is noted that the term 'ilm' appears in about 400 places indicating human knowledge, while the rest indicate the knowledge of Allah Almighty, whereas the term 'ma'rifa' is limited to human knowledge (3). And due to this clear interest in 'ilm and ma'rifa in the Noble Quran, there is an urgent need to know how to engage with the Quran because of its civilizational importance in the field of knowledge. Some scholars have devoted a comprehensive book to this topic, covering issues related to this aspect, nearly encompassing the intellectual, emotional, and behavioral etiquettes (4).
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage establishes the Quran's foundational emphasis on knowledge using evidence from verses and frequency analysis. The author cites three Quranic verses: first, a verse asserting that Allah, angels, and people of knowledge uphold justice; second, a verse promising elevated ranks for believers who are given knowledge; third, a verse contrasting the knowledgeable (who see the truth) with the ignorant (who are blind). The author then notes that the Quran mentions knowledge before and after creation in Surah Ar-Rahman. The quantitative data shows that the root 'alima' appears ~850 times, 'arafa' ~71 times, and 'ilm' is used ~400 times for human knowledge versus divine knowledge, while 'ma'rifa' is exclusively human. This data supports the assertion that the Quran prioritizes knowledge, leading to the need for proper methods of engaging with the Quran.

Two Main Directions: Knowledge as Power or Product of Thinking?
Author contrasts two educational views on knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two main educational directions regarding knowledge and map them to Islamic educational traditions.

Core Idea
The first direction views knowledge as power; the second sees it as product of thinking - two poles of educational epistemology.

This passage from an epistemological text identifies two contrasting views among educators: one treats knowledge as an end in itself, the other as a means to develop thinking. In Islamic education, these correspond to prioritising transmission of revealed knowledge versus nurturing critical ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two directions
Look for the sentences beginning with 'الاتجاه الأول' and 'الاتجاه الثاني'. Note the exact phrases: 'المعرفة قوة' vs 'المعرفة محصلة للتفكير'.
2
Find the philosophical labels
The text associates the first with essentialism and perennialism, the second with pragmatism and progressivism. Write down these schools.
3
Compare underlying assumptions
For the first direction, education aims to transmit knowledge as an end. For the second, education aims to develop thinking, with knowledge as a byproduct. Contrast their implied pedagogical methods.
4
Relate to Islamic educational traditions
In Islamic history, the emphasis on memorization (tahfiz) of Quran and Hadith aligns with the first direction. The emphasis on ijtihad and rational debate in Kalam and Usul al-Fiqh aligns with the second. Identify examples from each tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن هناك طرقاً مختلفة لبلوغ الحقيقة، إلا أن الموقف من معرفتها يظل مرتبطاً بموقف التربية من المعرفة بصرف النظر عن موقف النظريات التربوية المختلفة في كيفية الوصول إلى معرفة الحقيقة بين مغال في الاعتماد على الحس، أفضى به إلى الاعتقاد بعدم الحاجة إلى صوغ نظرية تربوية في المعرفة، وبين معتدل يركز اهتمامه على المشاركة الفاعلة للمتعلم في طبيعة الشيء المدروس. وبسبب من هذه الاختلافات فئة اتجاهان رئيسان عند المربين في نظرتهم إلى علاقة المعرفة بالتربية وهذان الاتجاهان هما: الاتجاه الأول يعدّ المعرفة قوة، وذلك بالنظر إلى أن الهدف الرئيس من التربية هو تحصيل المعرفة والمادة الدراسية تمتلك قيمة ذاتية بما تتضمنه من معرفة تساعد التلميذ على اكتشاف الحقيقة وهذه هي نظرة الفلسفة الجوهرية والتوارثية. الاتجاه الثاني: ويعد المعرفة محصلة للتفكير، وذلك من منطلق أن هدف التربية الوحيد هو مساعدة التلميذ على التفكير، وذلك مذهب البراجماتية الذرائعية والتقدمية القائلة بأن المعرفة ليست إلا محصلة للتفكير. ولعل مردّ ذلك الخلاف يعود إلى أسباب ثلاثة رئيسة: السبب الأول: أن نظرية المعرفة تمثل المفتاح الأساسي لفهم التربية عند أي تيار فلسفي، فيصبح اختلاف الاتجاهات المتعددة إنما هو انبثاق عن الاختلاف في نظريات المعرفة، لكونها تؤثر على البناء الفكري لكل تيار، فتأتي مسائل الكون وعلاقة الإنسان به والطبيعة البشرية والأهداف، والقيم، وسواها امتداداً لنظريته في المعرفة. السبب الثاني: أن هناك اختلافاً قائماً أصلاً في الدراسات الفلسفية والأبحاث المعرفية القديم منها والمعاصر في مرجعية الجذور والنظريات التي يتبناها هذا الباحث أو ذاك، مما يضفي على الأبحاث الإبستمولوجية المعاصرة طابعاً إيديولوجياً واضحاً. ومعروف أن الفكرة إذا طبعت بالإيديولوجيا تشبث كل باحث، أو فريق بما لديه، على نحو لا يسمح بتنازل أو تقارب مع الطرف الأخر على حساب إيديولوجيته. غير أن هذا لا يتناول في حقيقة الأمر كل الإيديولوجيات، بل يتناول فقط ما كان منها يقينياً قطعياً أو دوجماتياً. السبب الثالث: أن نظرية المعرفة تمثل موضوعاً من المواضيع المعقدة التي تتطلب تدقيقاً وتمحيصاً. ومن قبيل التسطيح الاقتصار على القول: بأن نظرية المعرفة لا تعدو أن تكون تحليلاً منطقياً للمعرفة، فإن هذا تعريف ناقص، وذلك لأن المعرفة ليست أمراً بسيطاً بعيداً عن التعقيد والغموض النسبي. هذا ويمكن أن يتحدد دور نظرية المعرفة في التربية من خلال تحقيق الأهداف الآتية: أولا: تجيب عن أسئلة المربين ومخططي المناهج حين يطرحون أسئلة من نوع: ماذا نعلّم؟ وما أنماط المعرفة التي نقدمها؟ ولماذا نختار هذا النوع من المعرفة دون الآخر؟ ثانيا: تبصر التربويين بضرورة مراعاتهم لطبيعة المعرفة، ومدى ملائمتها لأي من المراحل التعليمية، لاختيار المناسب منها لكل مستوى تعليمي، مع اختيار أفضل الأساليب لتقديمها.
There are different ways to reach the truth, but the stance on knowing it remains linked to the stance of education on knowledge, regardless of the stance of different educational theories on how to reach knowledge of the truth, between an extremist in relying on the senses, which led him to believe there is no need to formulate an educational theory of knowledge, and a moderate who focuses his attention on the active participation of the learner in the nature of the studied thing. Because of these differences, there are two main directions among educators in their view of the relationship between knowledge and education. These two directions are: The first direction considers knowledge as power, in view of the fact that the main goal of education is the acquisition of knowledge, and the subject matter possesses intrinsic value due to the knowledge it contains that helps the student discover the truth. This is the view of essentialist and perennialist philosophy. The second direction: It considers knowledge as a product of thinking, based on the premise that the sole goal of education is to help the student think. This is the doctrine of pragmatism, instrumentalism, and progressivism, which states that knowledge is nothing but a product of thinking. Perhaps the reason for this disagreement goes back to three main reasons: The first reason: The theory of knowledge represents the basic key to understanding education in any philosophical current, so the difference among multiple directions is an outgrowth of differences in theories of knowledge, because they affect the intellectual structure of each current. Thus, issues of the universe, man's relationship to it, human nature, goals, values, and others come as extensions of its theory of knowledge. The second reason: There is a pre-existing difference in philosophical studies and cognitive research, ancient and contemporary, in the reference of the roots and theories adopted by this or that researcher, which gives contemporary epistemological research a clear ideological character. It is known that if an idea is stamped with ideology, every researcher or group clings to what they have, in a way that does not allow concession or rapprochement with the other party at the expense of their ideology. However, this does not in reality address all ideologies, but only those that were certain, definitive, or dogmatic. The third reason: The theory of knowledge represents one of the complex topics that require scrutiny and investigation. It is a kind of superficiality to limit oneself to saying that the theory of knowledge is nothing but a logical analysis of knowledge, for this is an incomplete definition, because knowledge is not a simple matter far from complexity and relative ambiguity. The role of the theory of knowledge in education can be determined through achieving the following goals: First: It answers the questions of educators and curriculum planners when they ask questions like: What do we teach? What patterns of knowledge do we present? Why do we choose this type of knowledge over another? Second: It enlightens educators about the necessity of observing the nature of knowledge and its suitability for any of the educational stages, to choose the appropriate one for each educational level, along with choosing the best methods to present it.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage from the first chapter of the book discusses the development of epistemological theory, focusing on its relationship to education. The author begins by noting the diversity of approaches to attaining truth, yet the stance on knowing it is tied to educational theories. There is a spectrum from sensory extremism (which denies the need for a theory) to moderate activism (emphasizing learner participation). Two main educational directions emerge: the first views knowledge as power, associating with essentialist and perennialist philosophies where knowledge has intrinsic value and education aims to transmit it. The second sees knowledge as a product of thinking, linked to pragmatism and progressivism, where education's goal is to develop thinking skills. For example, in Islamic education, the first direction aligns with traditions that prioritize memorization of Quran and Hadith as foundational knowledge, while the second emphasizes ijtihad and critical reasoning. The author then identifies three reasons for this disagreement: first, epistemology fundamentally shapes educational theory, so differences in epistemology produce divergent educational approaches. Second, competing philosophical traditions carry ideological commitments that hinder compromise, especially when dogmatic. Third, epistemology itself is complex, not merely logical analysis of knowledge—it is intertwined with broader metaphysical and ethical questions. Finally, the role of epistemology in education is practical: it answers curricular questions ('what to teach?', 'why?') and guides age-appropriate content and methods.

Key Terms
نظرية المعرفة (nazariyyat al-ma'rifa): In this text, it is the philosophical study of knowledge that influences educational approaches, curriculum design, and the selection of teaching methods. [Note: Standard term in modern philosophy; stable across the tradition.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which philosophical tradition is associated with the view that knowledge is a product of thinking?
A) Essentialism
B) Perennialism
C) Pragmatism
D) Realism

Key Takeaway
Understanding whether one views knowledge as an end or as a tool for thinking shapes the entire educational approach.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether the traditional approach to teaching Hadith (e.g., al-Bukhari's method of collecting and transmitting hadith) aligns more with the first or second direction. Justify your answer using the criteria from the passage.
?
Find an example from the history of Islamic philosophy (e.g., Ibn Rushd vs. al-Ghazali) where differing views on knowledge as power vs. product of thinking led to educational disagreements.

Three Reasons for Epistemological Disagreement in Education
Author lists three reasons for disagreement on knowledge-education relationship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three reasons the author gives for why educators disagree on the relationship between knowledge and education.

Core Idea
Three factors — epistemology as foundational, ideological entrenchment, and the complexity of knowledge — drive educational disagreements.

After presenting two directions, the author gives three reasons for the persistent disagreement among educators. These reasons are not just theoretical; they are at play in Islamic intellectual history, where different epistemological commitments led to distinct curricula and pedagogical priorities.

Guided Path
1
List the three reasons
Match each 'السبب' in the text to its content. Write them down in order.
2
Explain each reason in your own words
For reason one: different epistemologies yield different educational theories. Reason two: ideological commitments block compromise. Reason three: epistemology is inherently complex.
3
Find Islamic historical examples
For each reason, provide an example from the Islamic tradition. E.g., reason one: Ash'ari vs. Mu'tazili epistemologies led to different emphases in education. Reason two: the Hanbali vs. Ash'ari debates on the nature of the Quran. Reason three: the complexity of the concept of 'ilm in Islamic philosophy.
4
Assess the author's claim
Do you agree that these three reasons sufficiently explain educational disagreements? What might be missing?

على الحس، أفضى به إلى الاعتقاد بعدم الحاجة إلى صوغ نظرية تربوية في المعرفة، وبين معتدل يركز اهتمامه على المشاركة الفاعلة للمتعلم في طبيعة الشيء المدروس. وبسبب من هذه الاختلافات فئة اتجاهان رئيسان عند تتضمنه من معرفة تساعد التلميذ على اكتشاف الحقيقة وهذه هي نظرة الفلسفة الجوهرية والتوارثية. الاتجاه الثاني: ويعد المعرفة محصلة للتفكير، وذلك من منطلق أن هدف التربية الوحيد هو مساعدة التلميذ على التربية عند أي تيار فلسفي، فيصبح اختلاف الاتجاهات المتعددة إنما هو انبثاق عن الاختلاف في نظريات المعرفة، لكونها تؤثر على البناء الفكري لكل تيار، فتأتي مسائل الكون وعلاقة الإنسان به والطبيعة البشرية والأهداف، والقيم، وسواها امتداداً لنظريته في المعرفة. السبب الثاني: أن هناك اختلافاً قائماً أصلاً في الدراسات الفلسفية والأبحاث المعرفية القديم منها والمعاصر في مرجعية الجذور والنظريات التي يتبناها هذا الباحث أو ذاك، مما يضفي على الأبحاث الإبستمولوجية المعاصرة طابعاً إيديولوجياً واضحاً. ومعروف أن الفكرة إذا طبعت بالإيديولوجيا تشبث كل باحث، أو فريق بما لديه، على نحو لا يسمح بتنازل أو تقارب مع الطرف الأخر على حساب إيديولوجيته. غير أن هذا لا يتناول في حقيقة الأمر كل الإيديولوجيات، بل يتناول فقط ما كان منها يقينياً قطعياً أو دوجماتياً. السبب الثالث: أن نظرية المعرفة تمثل موضوعاً من المواضيع التي نقدمها؟ ولماذا نختار هذا النوع من المعرفة دون الآخر؟ ثانيا: تبصر التربويين بضرورة مراعاتهم لطبيعة المعرفة، ومدى ملائمتها لأي من المراحل التعليمية، لاختيار المناسب منها لكل مستوى تعليمي، مع اختيار أفضل الأساليب لتقديمها.
There are different ways to reach the truth, but the stance on knowing it remains linked to the stance of education on knowledge, regardless of the stance of different educational theories on how to reach knowledge of the truth, between an extremist in relying on the senses, which led him to believe there is no need to formulate an educational theory of knowledge, and a moderate who focuses his attention on the active participation of the learner in the nature of the studied thing. Because of these differences, there are two main directions among educators in their view of the relationship between knowledge and education. These two directions are: The first direction considers knowledge as power, in view of the fact that the main goal of education is the acquisition of knowledge, and the subject matter possesses intrinsic value due to the knowledge it contains that helps the student discover the truth. The Practical Role of Epistemology in Educational Planning
Author explains the practical role of epistemology in education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how epistemology answers practical educational questions about curriculum content and pedagogy.

Core Idea
Epistemology guides educators in choosing what to teach and how to teach it.

The passage concludes by outlining the practical role of epistemology: it answers the 'what' and 'why' of curriculum and helps select appropriate methods for different levels. In Islamic education, this translates to decisions about what 'ulūm (sciences) to prioritize and at what stage.

Guided Path
1
Extract the two goals
From the text, identify the two roles of epistemology in education, introduced by 'أولا' and 'ثانيا'.
2
Reformulate as questions
The first role answers: 'What should we teach?' The second answers: 'How should we teach it according to the learner's level?'
3
Apply to Islamic curriculum
For the first, consider the classical division of 'ulūm into sharʿiyya (religious) and ʿaqliyya (rational). For the second, think about the sequence: Quran first, then Hadith, then Fiqh, then Kalam, etc.
4
Evaluate
Are these two roles sufficient? What other factors (e.g., social, political) might influence curriculum choices?

Ideology and Dogmatism in Epistemological Disputes
Author discusses the ideological source of epistemological disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of ideology and dogmatism in shaping epistemological disagreements.

Core Idea
Dogmatic ideology, not all ideology, blocks compromise in epistemology.

The author explains that epistemological research is often colored by deep-seated ideological commitments. This lesson focuses on the second reason for complexity: researchers cling to their own theories like ideologies, especially dogmatic ones, making genuine dialogue difficult.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about ideological imprinting
Find where the author says that epistemological research is imprinted with an ideological character. Notice the phrase 'طابعاً إيديولوجياً واضحاً'.
2
Distinguish between general ideology and dogmatic ideology
The author states that not all ideologies prevent concession—only those that are 'يقينياً قطعياً أو دوجماتياً' (certain and definitive or dogmatic). Differentiate between flexible ideologies and dogmatic ones.
Dogmatism holds that certainty is attainable and opposing views are false.
3
Analyze how dogmatism prevents compromise
When a researcher is dogmatic, they refuse to compromise on their ideological beliefs, even in the face of evidence. This creates entrenched positions.
4
Apply to an Islamic epistemological debate
Consider the historical debate between Ash'ari and Mu'tazili schools on divine attributes. Identify dogmatic elements that made compromise difficult.
Example: The Mu'tazili insistence on justice as a rational principle led to dogmatic rejection of certain hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السبب الثاني: أن هناك اختلافاً قائماً أصلاً في الدراسات الفلسفية والأبحاث المعرفية القديم منها والمعاصر في مرجعية الجذور والنظريات التي يتبناها هذا الباحث أو ذاك، مما يضفي على الأبحاث الإبستمولوجية المعاصرة طابعاً إيديولوجياً واضحاً. ومعروف أن الفكرة إذا طبعت بالإيديولوجيا تشبث كل باحث، أو فريق بما لديه، على نحو لا يسمح بتنازل أو تقارب مع الطرف الأخر على حساب إيديولوجيته. غير أن هذا لا يتناول في حقيقة الأمر كل الإيديولوجيات، بل يتناول فقط ما كان منها يقينياً قطعياً أو دوجماتياً (Dogmatism).
السبب الثالث: أن نظرية المعرفة تمثل موضوعاً من المواضيع المعقدة التي تتطلب تدقيقاً وتمحيصاً. ومن قبيل التسطيح الاقتصار على القول: بأن نظرية المعرفة لا تعدو أن تكون تحليلاً منطقياً للمعرفة، فإن هذا تعريف ناقص، وذلك لأن المعرفة ليست أمراً بسيطاً بعيداً عن التعقيد والغموض النسبي. هذا حتى ويمكن أن يتحدد دور نظرية المعرفة في التربية من خلال تحقيق الأهداف الآتية:
-١- تجيب عن أسئلة المربين ومخططي المناهج حين يطرحون أسئلة من نوع: ماذا نعلّم؟ وما أنماط المعرفة التي نقدمها؟ ولماذا نختار هذا النوع من المعرفة دون الآخر؟
٢- تبصر التربويين بضرورة مراعاتهم لطبيعة المعرفة، ومدى ملائمتها لأي من المراحل التعليمية، لاختيار المناسب منها لكل مستوى تعليمي، مع اختيار أفضل الأساليب لتقديمها.
-٣- تساعد التربية في التأكيد على طرائق المعرفة المختلفة وحياً، أو عقلاً، أو حدساً، أو تجريباً، بالصورة التي تُبرز وحدة المعرفة وتكاملها على نحو يعطى فيه كل جانب الاهتمام الذي يستحق.
٤ - تسهم في الكشف عن الأهمية التي تحتلها المعرفة الإنسانية من خلال تقويمها للمناهج والبرامج الدراسية في المواقف التعليمية والنشاطات الهادفة إلى التربية، وفي تبيين ما يصلح من الميراث والتجربة الإنسانية بما يتفق وفلسفة المجتمع.
وإذا كان هذا هو دور المعرفة في التربية بصورة عامة فإن الأساس المعرفي للمنهج يتصل بفلسفة المعرفة التي يتبناها المجتمع ويقدمها لأبنائه المتعلمين، كما يعبر عنها بمحتوى المواد التعليمية.
وفي ضوء كل ما تقدم، وحيث إن المعرفة أساسية في عملية النمو الإنساني، فإن نظرية المعرفة يجب أن تصبح جزءاً من أي فلسفة تربوية سليمة. إن هذه الفلسفة التربوية تتشكل من جملة عناصر هي عناصر المعرفة. ومع أن حول هذه العناصر مما لم يحسم - ولا أظنه سيحسم – بيد أن ذلك لا يحول دون الوقوف على بعض ما قيل فيها، حيث إن بعض الباحثين يوصل هذه العناصر إلى ستة على النحو التالي:
١- الحقائق.
٢ - المفاهيم.
المبادئ.
The second reason: There is a fundamental difference existing originally in philosophical studies and cognitive research, both ancient and contemporary, regarding the reference of the roots and theories adopted by this or that researcher, which gives contemporary epistemological research a clear ideological character. It is well known that if an idea is imprinted with ideology, every researcher or group clings to what they have in a manner that does not allow concession or convergence with the other party at the expense of their ideology. However, this does not in fact include all ideologies, but only those that are certain and definitive or dogmatic.
The third reason: That epistemology represents a subject of complex topics that require precision and scrutiny. It is a form of simplification to limit oneself to saying that epistemology is nothing but a logical analysis of knowledge, for this is an incomplete definition, because knowledge is not a simple matter far from complexity and relative ambiguity. This even though the role of epistemology in education can be determined through achieving the following objectives:
1. It answers the questions of educators and curriculum planners when they pose questions of the type: What do we teach? What patterns of knowledge do we present? Why do we choose this type of knowledge over another?
2. It enlightens educators about the necessity of taking into account the nature of knowledge and its suitability for any of the educational stages, to choose the appropriate one for each educational level, while selecting the best methods to present it.
3. It helps education in emphasizing the different methods of knowledge: revelation, reason, intuition, or experimentation, in a way that highlights the unity and integration of knowledge, giving each aspect the attention it deserves.
4. It contributes to revealing the importance that human knowledge occupies through its evaluation of curricula and study programs in educational situations and activities aimed at education, and in clarifying what is suitable from human heritage and experience in accordance with the philosophy of society.
And if this is the role of knowledge in education in general, then the cognitive foundation of the curriculum is connected to the philosophy of knowledge that society adopts and presents to its educated children, as expressed in the content of educational materials.
In light of all the foregoing, and since knowledge is fundamental to the process of human development, epistemology must become part of any sound educational philosophy. This educational philosophy is formed from a set of elements that are the elements of knowledge. Although there is no agreement on these elements – and I do not think it will be settled – yet that does not prevent us from looking at some of what has been said about them, as some researchers list these elements as six as follows:
1. Facts.
2. Concepts.
Principles.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion from a modern work, outlining two reasons for the complexity of epistemological studies and then detailing the role of epistemology in education. The author begins by presenting the second reason: the ingrained ideological differences in philosophical and cognitive research. Because each researcher or group is committed to their own ideological framework, compromise becomes difficult, especially when the ideology is dogmatic. The third reason is that epistemology itself is a complex subject; reducing it to a simple logical analysis of knowledge is insufficient. The author then shifts to the practical role of epistemology in education, listing four objectives. First, epistemology helps answer fundamental curriculum questions about what to teach and why. Second, it guides educators in matching knowledge types to appropriate educational levels and methods. Third, it emphasizes the various sources of knowledge—revelation, reason, intuition, and experimentation—promoting their integration. Fourth, it evaluates curricula and human experience to align with societal philosophy. The author concludes that epistemology must be integral to any sound educational philosophy, and mentions that knowledge comprises six elements, beginning with facts, concepts, and principles (the list is cut off).

Key Terms
إيديولوجيا
دوجماتية
يقينياً قطعياً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of ideology prevents concession between researchers?
A) All ideologies
B) Dogmatic ideologies only
C) Secular ideologies
D) Religious ideologies

Key Takeaway
Dogmatic ideology, not ideology in general, creates epistemological rigidity and hinders scholarly compromise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a contemporary debate in Islamic thought where ideological commitments prevent compromise (e.g., between traditionalist and reformist scholars). Describe how dogmatism plays a role based on the passage's distinction.

Knowledge's Complexity Beyond Logical Analysis
Author argues that epistemology is complex and cannot be reduced to logical analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to argue why epistemology cannot be reduced to a mere logical analysis of knowledge.

Core Idea
Knowledge is complex and relative, making a purely logical analysis incomplete.

The author presents the third reason for the complexity of epistemology: knowledge is not a simple matter. Reducing it to logical analysis is a form of simplification that ignores its depth. This lesson unpacks that critique and its implications for Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's target: the reductionist definition
Find where the author criticizes the view that epistemology is 'تحليلاً منطقياً للمعرفة' (a logical analysis of knowledge). Note the word 'تسطيح' (simplification).
This definition is labeled as incomplete ('تعريف ناقص').
2
Extract the reasons for complexity
The author states that knowledge is not simple but involves 'تعقيد' (complexity) and 'غموض نسبي' (relative ambiguity). These suggest multiple dimensions: sources, validation, and context.
Later in the passage, sources like revelation, reason, intuition, and experimentation are mentioned.
3
Connect to Islamic epistemology
In Islamic thought, knowledge includes categories like 'ilm (certain knowledge) and zann (conjecture), and sources include the Qur'an, sunna, reason, and empirical experience. A purely logical approach would miss the revelatory dimension.
Example: The usul al-fiqh principle of qiyas (analogy) combines logic with scriptural authority.
4
Assess the implications for curriculum development
If knowledge is complex, educators must consider various types and sources when designing curricula. The author uses this to transition into the educational role of epistemology.

Epistemology's Four Educational Objectives
Author lists four educational roles of epistemology and links them to curriculum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the four educational objectives of epistemology to curriculum design and teaching methods.

Core Idea
Epistemology answers what, why, and how we teach, integrating multiple sources of knowledge.

The author transitions from the complexity of knowledge to the practical role of epistemology in education. He lists four specific objectives that epistemology fulfills for educators and curriculum planners. This lesson breaks down each objective and shows how they can guide Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
List the four objectives from the passage
Identify the four numbered points in the Arabic. They begin with 'تجيب عن أسئلة المربين' and end with 'بما يتفق وفلسفة المجتمع'.
The author uses 'يتحدد دور نظرية المعرفة في التربية من خلال تحقيق الأهداف الآتية'.
2
Explain each objective in your own words
Objective 1: Answers educators' questions about what to teach and why. Objective 2: Guides age-appropriate knowledge and methods. Objective 3: Emphasizes multiple knowledge sources (revelation, reason, intuition, experimentation) and their integration. Objective 4: Evaluates curricula and human experience against societal philosophy.
3
Connect to Islamic educational practice
For example, Objective 3 directly applies to Islamic seminaries that teach tafsir (revelation), usul al-fiqh (reason), tasawwuf (intuition), and experimental sciences. Integration is key.
Object 4: Evaluating which aspects of Islamic heritage are suitable for modern society requires epistemological reflection.
4
Discuss the foundation of the curriculum in epistemology
The passage concludes that epistemology must be part of any sound educational philosophy, and that curriculum elements (facts, concepts, principles) derive from epistemological choices.
This links back to the complexity: educators must be aware of the nature of knowledge they teach.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

2. It enlightens educators about the necessity of taking into account the nature of knowledge and its suitability for any of the educational stages, to choose the appropriate one for each educational level, while selecting the best methods to present it.
3. It helps education in emphasizing the different methods of knowledge: revelation, reason, intuition, or experimentation, in a way that highlights the unity and integration of knowledge, giving each aspect the attention it deserves.
4. It contributes to revealing the importance that human knowledge occupies through its evaluation of curricula and study programs in educational situations and activities aimed at education, and in clarifying what is suitable from human heritage and experience in accordance with the philosophy of society.
And if this is the role of knowledge in education in general, then the cognitive foundation of the curriculum is connected to the philosophy of knowledge that society adopts and presents to its educated children, as expressed in the content of educational materials.
In light of all the foregoing, and since knowledge is fundamental to the process of human development, epistemology must become part of any sound educational philosophy. This educational philosophy is formed from a set of elements that are the elements of knowledge. Although there is no agreement on these elements – and I do not think it will be settled – yet that does not prevent us from looking at some of what has been said about them, as some researchers list these elements as six as follows:
1. Facts.
2. Concepts.
Principles.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion from a modern work, outlining two reasons for the complexity of epistemological studies and then detailing the role of epistemology in education. The author begins by presenting the second reason: the ingrained ideological differences in philosophical and cognitive research. Because each researcher or group is committed to their own ideological framework, compromise becomes difficult, especially when the ideology is dogmatic. The third reason is that epistemology itself is a complex subject; reducing it to a simple logical analysis of knowledge is insufficient. The author then shifts to the practical role of epistemology in education, listing four objectives. First, epistemology helps answer fundamental curriculum questions about what to teach and why. Second, it guides educators in matching knowledge types to appropriate educational levels and methods. Third, it emphasizes the various sources of knowledge—revelation, reason, intuition, and experimentation—promoting their integration. Fourth, it evaluates curricula and human experience to align with societal philosophy. The author concludes that epistemology must be integral to any sound educational philosophy, and mentions that knowledge comprises six elements, beginning with facts, concepts, and principles (the list is cut off).

Author presents two classifications of knowledge elements from an Islamic educational perspective.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and compare the two classifications of knowledge elements in Islamic education as presented in the passage.

Core Idea
Islamic education organizes knowledge into distinct elements, from facts to faith.

This passage presents two complementary frameworks for understanding the building blocks of knowledge in education. By examining both the six-element taxonomy from general educational theory and the four-element Quranic model, you will see how epistemology shapes curriculum design and development.

4- It contributes to revealing the importance of human knowledge through evaluating curricula and study programs in educational situations and activities aimed at education, and in clarifying what is suitable from human heritage and experience in accordance with the philosophy of society (1).
If this is the role of knowledge in education in general, then the cognitive foundation of the curriculum is connected to the philosophy of knowledge that the society adopts and presents to its learners, as expressed in the content of educational materials (2).
In light of all the foregoing, and since knowledge is fundamental in the process of human development, epistemology must become part of any sound educational philosophy (3). This educational philosophy is composed of a set of elements which are the elements of knowledge. Although there is no consensus on these elements - and I do not think there will be - that does not prevent us from reviewing some of what has been said about them, as some researchers list these elements as six, as follows:
1- Facts.
2- Concepts.
Principles.
(1) Salih Dhiyab Hindi and colleagues, Curriculum Planning and Development, p. 142.
(2) Ibid., p. 137.
(3) Phenix, Philosophy of Education, p. 468, and see: The Effective School Curriculum by Jawdat Ahmad Sa'ada and Abdullah Muhammad Ibrahim, pp. 261-295.
4- Skills.
5- Laws and norms.
6- Methods of acquiring knowledge (1).
It is clear that this is an educational classification based on a systematic process that assumes the curriculum must include facts, and connect them with mental processes, values, attitudes, and inclinations that the curriculum aims to develop in the learner. Also, knowledge of the concept as an abstract element is not possible unless the learner knows what this concept indicates. Likewise, principles are a main idea or truth upon which other ideas can be built when designing the curriculum, and in the learner's behavior. As for skills, the task of the curriculum is to develop educational and pedagogical skills such as learning reading, writing, and various other skills. Similarly, regarding the element of laws and norms, the goal of the educational curriculum is to study the universe and society so that the learner understands the laws governing each. Finally, methods of acquiring knowledge mean giving each knowledge its research methodology. History examines topics using the historical method, and so on (2).
Likewise, some educational researchers have summarized the elements of knowledge in Quranic education, concerned with human life present and future, into four:
1- Faith.
2- Character.
Knowledge.
- Action (3).
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about the role of knowledge in education and the classification of its elements. It begins by highlighting how education emphasizes different methods of knowledge acquisition: revelation, reason, intuition, and experimentation, aiming to show their integration. The author then states that the cognitive basis of the curriculum is tied to the society's philosophy of knowledge. Since knowledge is essential for human development, epistemology must be part of any sound educational philosophy. The author notes that there is no consensus on the elements of knowledge, but presents one classification by some researchers into six elements: facts, concepts, principles, skills, laws and norms, and methods of acquiring knowledge. The author explains each element: facts are to be included in the curriculum and connected to mental processes; concepts are abstract and require the learner to know their referents; principles are foundational ideas for building other ideas; skills are to be developed through education; laws and norms involve studying the universe and society; methods of acquiring knowledge assign each discipline its own research methodology (e.g., history uses the historical method). Then, the author presents another classification from Quranic education, which summarizes the elements into four: faith, character, knowledge, and action. This second classification is concerned with human life in the present and future. The passage is descriptive and classificatory, not argumentative.

Understanding Theory and Its Two Types
Author defines theory and its two types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between explanatory-predictive and practical theories and identify the common element they share.

Core Idea
A theory is both an explanation of phenomena and a practical activity rooted in knowledge and belief.

In this passage, the author sets the stage by defining 'theory' and immediately classifying it into two types. This distinction is crucial for understanding how theories function in Islamic sciences—whether they aim to explain why things are as they are (explanatory-predictive) or to guide practice (practical). Let's walk through the author's analytical steps.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of theory
Locate the definition: theory is what corresponds to partial scientific facts, interpreted as an explanation of phenomena, like the atomic theory.
2
Distinguish the two types
The passage explicitly names two types: predictive explanatory theory (understanding cause) and practical theory (activity amenable to practice).
3
Find the common element
Both types include knowledge and belief. This is the unifying factor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يقابل الحقائق العلمية الجزئية، وهي تعني هنا تفسير عدة ظواهر من قبيل الفرضية العلمية، كما هو في نظرية الذرة. وفي ضوء هذه المعاني فإنه يجب التمييز بين نوعين من النظرية: النوع الأول نظرية تنبئية تفسيرية، أي محاولة فهم علة كون الأمور على ما هي عليه. والنوع الآخر نظرية عملية أي عبارة عن نشاط قابل للممارسة، ويجمع بين المعنيين اشتمالهما على معنى المعرفة والاعتقاد.
What corresponds to partial scientific facts, and it means here the interpretation of several phenomena such as the scientific hypothesis, as in the atomic theory. In light of these meanings, one must distinguish two types of theory: the first type is a predictive explanatory theory, i.e. an attempt to understand the cause of things being as they are. The other type is a practical theory, i.e. an activity amenable to practice. What brings the two meanings together is that both include the meaning of knowledge and belief.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'theory' and immediately classifies it into two types. It first equates theory with what corresponds to partial scientific facts, and clarifies that here it means the interpretation of phenomena, like the atomic theory in science. Then it explains that in light of these meanings, we must distinguish two types: predictive explanatory theory (which seeks to understand the cause of phenomena) and practical theory (which is an activity that can be practiced). The common element between them is that they both involve knowledge and belief. The passage thus provides a functional definition that serves as a foundation for further discussions in the book.

Dissecting the Definition of Educational Theory
Definition of educational theory as a compound concept.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the genus and differentiae in any definition of a theoretical concept using the example of educational theory.

Core Idea
A definition reveals a concept's genus and differentiae, making it analyzable.

This passage presents a definition of educational theory drawn from a researcher's synthesis. It shows how a theory is more than a loose collection of ideas — it is a structured set of concepts resting on explicit foundations, informed by data, and directed toward goals. In this lesson, we will dissect this definition using the logical tools of genus (jins) and differentia (fasl) to see how it achieves completeness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined in the Arabic. It is 'نظرية التربية' (educational theory). This is the thing we want to define.
2
Extract the genus
What broader category does the definiendum belong to? The passage says it is 'a set of educational concepts' (جملة من المفاهيم التربوية). That is the genus — the class to which educational theory belongs.
3
Extract the differentiae
What distinguishes this set of concepts from any other set? Three differentiae are given: (1) it is based on philosophical, religious, or social foundations, (2) it incorporates cultural and scientific data, (3) it has goals that allow the interpretation of organized educational processes.
4
Assess completeness
A complete definition must include all instances and exclude non-instances. Here, the differentiae ensure that only theories that rest on foundations, use data, and aim at interpreting processes are included. This seems comprehensive within the author's framework.
5
Classify the definition type
Is this a real definition (hadd haqiqi) or a description (rasm)? Since it lists components and functions rather than essential characteristics, it is likely a complete description (rasm taam).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريف نظرية التربية: وبعد أن ساق أحد الباحثين جملة تعريفات للنظرية التربوية بصورة عامة قال: إنها جملة من المفاهيم التربوية التي تقوم على مجموعة من المرتكزات الفلسفية أو الدينية أو الاجتماعية أو جميعها، مع المعطيات الثقافية والعلمية، ومجموعة من الأهداف التي يمكن في ضوئها تفسير كل العمليات التربوية المنظمة نظرياً ومنهجياً ونظامياً.
Definition of educational theory: After one researcher cited a set of definitions of educational theory in general, he said: It is a set of educational concepts based on a set of philosophical, religious, or social foundations, or all of them, along with cultural and scientific data, and a set of goals in light of which all educational processes can be interpreted, organized theoretically, methodologically, and systematically.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage provides a definition of educational theory as given by a researcher. It is a set of educational concepts that rest on philosophical, religious, or social foundations, combined with cultural and scientific data, and a set of goals. These goals allow the interpretation of all educational processes that are organized theoretically, methodologically, and systematically. This definition highlights the multi-dimensional nature of educational theory, linking it to diverse foundations and structured processes.

Key Takeaway
Every complete definition specifies a genus (what kind of thing it is) and one or more differentiae (what makes it distinct within that genus).

Defining Islamic Educational Theory and Critiquing Secular Classifications
Author defines Islamic educational theory and critiques a common division of theory types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare two definitions of Islamic educational theory and explain the author's critique of Moore's division into predictive-explanatory and directive-practical theories.

Core Idea
Islamic educational theory must be derived from the Qur'an and Sunnah, not from secular philosophical assumptions.

In this passage, the author presents two comprehensive definitions of Islamic educational theory and then critiques a common secular classification. Understanding these definitions is essential for anyone engaged in Islamic education, as they clarify the foundational principles that distinguish Islamic from non-Islamic educational theories. The author warns against adopting theories that assume Islamic education can be treated like any natural science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate the first definition starting with 'مجموعة من التصورات...' and the second starting with 'مجموعة مترابطة من المبادئ...'.
The first definition is more abstract; the second explicitly mentions Qur'an and Sunnah.
2
Extract key components of the first definition
Note that it includes perceptions, concepts, ideas, goals, rulings, values, with maximal abstraction, aimed at preparing the Muslim human, and in light of which educational processes are interpreted, justified, and evaluated.
3
Understand Moore's classification
The author reviews Moore's division into predictive-explanatory and directive-practical theories. Recognize that the first type assumes human sciences are like natural sciences, which the author rejects.
4
Analyze the critique
The author argues that the first type is problematic because it applies natural science methodology to human sciences uncritically. The second type must be controlled by Qur'an and Sunnah.
The critique is epistemological: the author rejects positivist assumptions.
5
Compare with the second definition
Note that the second definition explicitly bases the theory on Qur'an and Sunnah, providing a concrete alternative to the secular classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريف نظرية التربية الإسلامية: أما النظرية التربوية الإسلامية فثمة تعريفات عدة لها، ولكن يبدو أن من أشملها التعريف التالي: مجموعة من التصورات والمفاهيم والأفكار، والأهداف والأحكام والقيم ذات الحد الأقصى من التجريد والعمومية المرتبطة بإعداد الإنسان المسلم، حسب الأصول الإسلامية، وفي ضوئها يمكن تفسير العمليات التربوية الإسلامية وتبريرها وتقويمها، اعتباراً من أسسها ومناهجها وأساليب ووسائل تحقيقها وتنفيذها. وبمراجعة ما خلص إليه مور من كون النظرية قسمين: تفسيرية تنبئية وتوجيهية عملية. فإن الأولى تفترض أن العلوم الإنسانية والاجتماعية ومنها التربوية لا تختلف في منهجها عن العلوم الطبيعية والتجريبية، وهذا منطق لا يسلّم به وعليه مآخذ عدة. والأخرى يجب ضبطها ونقد ركائزها الفلسفية حتى لا تصبح مجرد إرشادات وتوجيهات تخضع للفلسفة السائدة أياً كان مصدرها. ولذلك فلا بد من تقييدها في إطار الكتاب والسنة. وقد عرَّفها أحد الباحثين في هذا الميدان بكونها: مجموعة مترابطة من المبادئ والقواعد والمفاهيم التربوية المستمدة من القرآن الكريم والسنة المطهرة، والتي هي بمثابة الأساس المتين، والذي يقوم عليه البناء التربوي الصالح.
Definition of Islamic educational theory: As for Islamic educational theory, there are several definitions of it, but it seems that one of the most comprehensive is the following: A set of perceptions, concepts, ideas, goals, rulings, and values of the maximum degree of abstraction and generality related to the preparation of the Muslim human being, according to Islamic principles, in light of which Islamic educational processes can be interpreted, justified, and evaluated, starting from its foundations, curricula, methods, and means of achieving and implementing them. Upon reviewing the conclusion of Moore that theory is of two types: predictive explanatory and directive practical, the first assumes that the human and social sciences – including education – do not differ in their methodology from the natural and experimental sciences, and this logic is not accepted and has several criticisms. The other type must be controlled and its philosophical foundations criticized so that it does not become mere guidance and directives subject to the prevailing philosophy whatever its source. Therefore, it must be restricted within the framework of the Qur'an and Sunnah. One researcher in this field defined it as: An interrelated set of principles, rules, and educational concepts derived from the Holy Qur'an and the purified Sunnah, which serve as the solid foundation upon which sound educational construction is based.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage deals with the definition of Islamic educational theory. It begins by noting that there are several definitions, but the most comprehensive is that it is a set of perceptions, concepts, ideas, goals, rulings, and values with maximal abstraction and generality, aimed at preparing the Muslim human according to Islamic principles, and in light of which all Islamic educational processes can be interpreted, justified, and evaluated. Then the author reviews Moore's classification of theory into predictive explanatory and directive practical. The critique is that the first type assumes human sciences follow the same method as natural sciences, which is not accepted and has many criticisms. The second type must be controlled and its philosophical foundations criticized to avoid being mere guidance subject to any prevailing philosophy. Therefore, it must be restricted to the framework of Qur'an and Sunnah. Finally, another researcher's definition is given: an interrelated set of principles, rules, and concepts derived from Qur'an and Sunnah, forming the solid foundation for sound educational construction.

Key Terms
النظرية التربوية الإسلامية (al-nazariyya al-tarbawiyya al-islamiyya): First definition: a set of perceptions, concepts, ideas, goals, rulings, and values of maximum abstraction and generality for preparing the Muslim human being, in light of which Islamic educational processes are interpreted, justified, and evaluated. Second definition: an interrelated set of principles, rules, and educational concepts derived from the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the essential source that must restrict Islamic educational theory?
A) Greek philosophy.
B) The prevailing philosophy.
C) The Qur'an and Sunnah.
D) Modern scientific methods.

Key Takeaway
Islamic educational theory must be rooted in the Qur'an and Sunnah to remain distinct from secular philosophical assumptions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Defining Theory of Knowledge in Islamic Epistemology
Author defines theory of knowledge as the study of principles, nature, and limits of human knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to dissect the Islamic definition of theory of knowledge into its constituent investigative domains and articulate the epistemological questions it addresses.

Core Idea
Theory of knowledge maps the territory of human knowing: its sources, limits, and relation to reality.

This passage presents a comprehensive definition of theory of knowledge (nazariyyat al-ma‘rifa) as understood in the Islamic intellectual tradition. The author builds on a preceding discussion of 'theory' in general and then specifies what the theory of knowledge investigates. You will work through the components of this definition to see how it frames the entire enterprise of Islamic epistemology, from the principles of knowledge to the correspondence between perceptions and reality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
The term being defined is 'نظرية المعرفة' (nazariyyat al-ma‘rifa). Notice how the author first reminds us of the general meaning of 'نظرية' (theory) before narrowing to this specific field.
2
Extract the investigative domains
List the eight elements mentioned: principles, nature, source, methods, value, limits, relation between subject and object, and correspondence of perceptions to reality. Each is a distinct topic within epistemology.
These correspond to key questions: What is knowledge? How is it acquired? What are its boundaries?
3
Analyze the subject-object relation
The definition explicitly includes 'the relationship between the perceiving subject and the perceived object'. This highlights that knowledge is not just a mental state but involves a real connection to an external world.
This rejects purely subjective accounts of knowledge.
4
Focus on the correspondence criterion
The author asks 'to what extent our perceptions correspond to what is actually taken, independent of the mind'. This establishes a realist theory of truth: knowledge must match reality.
This is the classic correspondence theory, foundational in Islamic epistemology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريف نظرية المعرفة: وإذا كانت تلك هي معاني النظرية، فإن نظرية المعرفة تبحث في مبادئ المعرفة الإنسانية وطبيعتها ومصدرها، وطرائقها وقيمتها وحدودها، وفي الصلة بين الذات المدركة والموضوع المدرك، وبيان إلى أي مدى تكون فيه تصوراتنا مطابقة لما يؤخذ فعلاً، مستقلاً عن الذهن.
Definition of theory of knowledge: If those are the meanings of theory, then the theory of knowledge investigates the principles of human knowledge, its nature, source, methods, value, and limits, and the relationship between the perceiving subject and the perceived object, and an explanation of the extent to which our perceptions correspond to what is actually taken, independent of the mind.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage defines the theory of knowledge. It connects to the previous discussion of theory in general, and specifies that theory of knowledge examines the principles, nature, source, methods, value, and limits of human knowledge. It also investigates the relationship between the perceiving subject and the perceived object, and explains to what extent our perceptions correspond to reality independent of the mind. This definition covers the main branches of epistemology.

Key Terms
نظرية المعرفة

Key Takeaway
Theory of knowledge in the Islamic tradition is a comprehensive study that includes not just the origin and nature of knowledge but also its limits and the crucial relationship between mind and reality.

Islamic Theory of Knowledge vs. Western Epistemology
Author compares Islamic theory of knowledge with Western epistemology and clarifies their relationship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Islamic theory of knowledge (nazariyyat al-ma'rifa) and Western epistemology based on their scope and foundational assumptions.

Core Idea
Islamic theory of knowledge is not synonymous with Western epistemology.

In the previous lesson, we established that Islamic theory of knowledge covers foundational questions about knowledge. Now the author compares this with Western epistemology, clarifying that while both study knowledge, they are not identical. This is crucial for avoiding conceptual confusion when engaging with modern philosophical discussions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question posed
The author asks: 'To what extent does Islamic theory of knowledge meet Western epistemology?' Recognize that this sets up a comparative analysis.
The question implies a distinction, not identity.
2
Examine the description of Western epistemology
The passage states that Western epistemology primarily involves analyzing and critiquing the results of natural and human sciences, acting as a philosophy of science.
This is a modern, Western academic discipline.
3
Note the broader categorization
Western epistemology is one of three branches of philosophy (ontology, axiology, epistemology). Contrast this with how Islamic theory of knowledge is rooted in revelation and Islamic sciences.
Islamic theory of knowledge is not a branch of philosophy in the same sense.
4
Recognize the warning
The author explicitly warns against using 'philosophy of knowledge' as synonymous with Islamic theory of knowledge. Understand that this conflation could distort Islamic concepts.
The terms are not interchangeable.
5
Synthesize the relationship
Islamic theory of knowledge and Western epistemology share some concerns (e.g., nature of knowledge) but differ in scope, sources, and ultimate aims. They are not identical or synonymous.
This distinction is essential for proper engagement with both traditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نظرية المعرفة والإبستمولوجيا (Epistemology)
وإذا تقرر أن نظرية المعرفة تتناول كل ما سبق فإلى أي مدى تلتقي مع الإبستمولوجيا الغربية؟
تجدر الإشارة ابتداء إلى أن الدراسات الإبستمولوجية إذ تتناول بالتحليل والنقد نتائج العلوم الطبيعية منها ،والإنسانية كإحدى اهتماماتها الرئيسة، فإنها تعني بذلك نوعاً من (فلسفة العلوم (). وبمعنى أوسع فإن من الممكن اعتبار الإبستمولوجيا نوعاً من الفلسفة العامة بوصفها إحدى المباحث الثلاثة للفلسفة: الوجود (ontology) والقيم (Oxeology) وكذلك المعرفة (Episetmogy). ولكن ذلك لا يعني جواز استخدام مصطلح فلسفة المعرفة باعتباره مرادفـاً
Theory of Knowledge and Epistemology. If it is settled that theory of knowledge covers all that was mentioned, to what extent does it meet Western epistemology? It is necessary to indicate from the beginning that epistemological studies, since they deal with analysis and critique of the results of the natural and human sciences as one of their main concerns, thereby represent a kind of 'philosophy of science'. In a broader sense, it is possible to consider epistemology as a type of general philosophy as one of the three branches of philosophy: ontology, axiology, and knowledge (epistemology). But that does not mean the permissibility of using the term 'philosophy of knowledge' as synonymous.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage opens a comparative discussion between Islamic theory of knowledge (nazariyyat al-ma'rifa) and Western epistemology. The author asks: to what extent do they converge? He notes that epistemological studies in the West involve analyzing and critiquing the results of natural and human sciences, essentially making it a kind of 'philosophy of science'. More broadly, epistemology can be considered one of the three branches of philosophy (ontology, axiology, epistemology). However, the author warns against equating the term 'philosophy of knowledge' (falsafat al-ma'rifa) with Islamic theory of knowledge, implying a critical stance toward uncritical adoption of Western terminology.

Key Terms
إبستمولوجيا (ibistimulujia): Western epistemology, which analyzes and critically evaluates the results of natural and human sciences, and is considered a branch of philosophy alongside ontology and axiology. [Note: This term is a modern loanword; not found in classical Islamic logic texts.]

Key Takeaway
Islamic theory of knowledge and Western epistemology have different scopes and foundations; equating them leads to conceptual confusion.

Two Views on Epistemology vs. Theory of Knowledge in French Thought
Author discusses two contrasting views on the relationship between epistemology and theory of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two French views on the relationship between theory of knowledge and epistemology and apply this distinction to Islamic epistemological discussions.

Core Idea
In French thought, epistemology is either a specific part of theory of knowledge or a completely separate historical analysis of science.

The relationship between theory of knowledge (nazariyya al-ma'rifa) and epistemology (al-ibistimulujiya) is not fixed. In the French context, two opposing views coexist. Understanding these views helps clarify how Islamic epistemology relates to broader philosophical frameworks. This lesson unpacks both views, preparing you to navigate similar conceptual distinctions in Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two views
Read the Arabic passage and locate the two opinions. The first opinion connects theory of knowledge (general) and epistemology (specific); the second opinion separates them entirely. Underline the key phrases that indicate connection vs. separation.
The first view uses 'اتصال' (connection) and 'انفصال' (separation) together; the second view insists on 'تميز' (distinction).
2
Extract the key differences
For each view, list the basis of the relationship. First view: theory of knowledge is general (nature, limits, possibility); epistemology is specific (abstract philosophical analysis). Second view: epistemology is not a theory of knowledge; it studies scientific thought historically, avoiding false generalizations.
The second view explicitly says 'الإبستمولوجيا ليست نظرية في المعرفة' (epistemology is not a theory of knowledge).
3
Assess alignment with Islamic thought
Consider how classical Islamic scholars like al-Ghazali or Ibn Rushd approached knowledge. Does their concept of 'nazariyya al-ma'rifa' include both general and specific aspects? Which French view is more compatible with the Islamic perspective?
Islamic epistemology often integrates metaphysical, empirical, and revelatory sources, which may align more with the first view's broad scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجدر قبل اختتام الحديث عن العلاقة بين نظرية المعرفة و الإبستمولوجيا أن أشير إلى رأيين - في هذا الصدد - ظاهرهما التعارض في إطار المعنى الفرنسي ذاته : الرأي الأول: إنه مهما قيل عن وجود خلاف بين نظرية المعرفة والإبستمولوجيا فإن اتصالاً وثيقاً يربط بينهما من جانب معنى نظرية المعرفة (العام) الذي يبحث في طبيعتها وحدودها وإمكان الحصول عليها، ومن جانب معنى الإبستمولوجيا الدقيق الخاص) كمظهر بارز على صعيد التحليل الفلسفي المجرّد أي إن هناك اتصالاً وانفصالاً بينهما، كما أن هناك عمومية أكثر لنظرية المعرفة، وخصوصية أدق للإبستمولوجيا الرأي الثاني: ويبني رأيه على أساس من تميز نظرية المعرفة في جميع المذاهب الفلسفية عن الإبستمولوجيا، ثم يخلص إلى القول: إن الإبستمولوجيا ليست نظرية في المعرفة؛ لأنها تحاول ألا تربط - مثل نظرية المعرفة - بالأهداف العامة لنسق فلسفي ما. ومن جهة ثانية فإن الإبستمولوجيا ليست جزءاً من نظرية المعرفة خاصاً بالبحث في المعرفة العملية، ذلك لأن الاختلاف الأساسي بين نظرية المعرفة والإبستمولوجيا هو أن الإبستمولوجيا لا هدف لها في بناء نظرية خاصة في المعرفة وأنها تتناول التفكير العلمي في مرحلة تاريخية من مراحل تطوره. ذلك أنها تريد أن تظل على وعي بتاريخه ونسبيته، لئلا تقع في خطأ التعميم الواهم للنتائج المحصلة
Before concluding the discussion on the relationship between theory of knowledge and epistemology, it is appropriate to refer to two opinions - in this regard - that appear contradictory within the same French meaning: The first opinion: No matter what is said about the existence of a disagreement between theory of knowledge and epistemology, a close connection links them from the aspect of the (general) meaning of theory of knowledge which examines its nature, limits, and the possibility of obtaining it, and from the aspect of the precise (specific) meaning of epistemology as a prominent manifestation at the level of abstract philosophical analysis. That is, there is connection and separation between them, just as there is more generality for theory of knowledge and more specificity for epistemology. The second opinion: It builds its view on the basis of the distinction of theory of knowledge in all philosophical schools from epistemology, then concludes that epistemology is not a theory of knowledge because it tries not to connect - like theory of knowledge - to the general goals of a philosophical system. On the other hand, epistemology is not a part of theory of knowledge specific to research on practical knowledge, because the fundamental difference between theory of knowledge and epistemology is that epistemology has no goal of building a specific theory of knowledge and that it deals with scientific thinking at a historical stage of its development. This is because it wants to remain aware of its history and relativity, so as not to fall into the error of false generalization of the results obtained.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents two contrasting views on the relationship between 'theory of knowledge' (nazariyya al-ma'rifa) and 'epistemology' (al-ibistimulujiya) within the French conceptual framework. The first view argues for a close connection while acknowledging differences: theory of knowledge is more general, studying the nature and limits of knowledge, while epistemology is more specific, focusing on abstract philosophical analysis. The second view insists on a clear separation, maintaining that epistemology is not a theory of knowledge because it avoids tying itself to a particular philosophical system and instead examines scientific thought historically, wary of overgeneralization. The author presents both views without endorsing either, setting the stage for further discussion.

Key Terms
نظرية المعرفة (nazariyya al-ma'rifa): The general philosophical study of the nature, limits, and possibility of knowledge. [Note: In Islamic thought, 'nazariyya al-ma'rifa' often refers to Islamic epistemology, which may differ from Western usage.]
الإبستمولوجيا (al-ibistimulujiya): The French concept of epistemology, often associated with philosophy of science and analysis of scientific knowledge. [Note: English 'epistemology' is broader, roughly equivalent to theory of knowledge; French usage is narrower.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The French debate shows that 'epistemology' can mean different things; Islamic epistemology must be defined precisely to avoid conceptual confusion.

Analyzing objections to calling Islam a 'theory'
Author presents objections and begins critique

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the reasons scholars give for rejecting the term 'theory' for Islam and evaluate the author's initial critique of those reasons.

Core Idea
Rejecting the term 'theory' for Islam may stem from a misunderstanding of what 'theory' means.

In this passage, the author presents several scholars who absolutely refuse to apply the word 'theory' to Islam. He quotes Sayyid Qutb and others who argue that the living Islamic creed cannot be reduced to an abstract theory. Then he begins to discuss the mistake in this position. We will analyze their arguments and see how the author starts to respond.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common stance
All the scholars quoted share an absolute rejection of using the term 'theory' (نظرية) for Islam or the Quran. Note the phrase 'رفض قاطع' (absolute rejection).
2
Extract each scholar's reasoning
Sayyid Qutb argues that Islam is a living creed to be embodied, not an abstract theory. An educational researcher says theory is a set of refutable principles, but Islamic education is irrefutable. Another researcher questions whether human terms can apply to Islam at all.
Pay attention to the different grounds: theological, methodological, and linguistic.
3
Locate the author's critique
The author begins a section titled 'Discussion of the Cautious Opinions: The Mistake'. He acknowledges Qutb's depth but indicates that even great researchers can err. The text cuts off, but the author sets out to show that the rejection is misguided.
4
Evaluate the objections' validity
Consider whether a term like 'theory' must always be abstract and refutable. Could it be used in a broader sense to mean a systematic body of teachings? The author seems poised to argue that the term can be applied if properly defined.
This prepares you for the author's full argument in later lessons.

Definition of Theory in the Quran. He answers that: 'The reality is that we cannot apply the term theory to Islam, even though it contains among what it contains what humans have agreed upon and have conventionally called theory.' Commentary
This passage is a critical presentation of arguments against using the term 'theory' for Islam. The author first introduces the problem: disagreement over terms leads some to absolutely reject applying 'theory' to the Quran. He then quotes Sayyid Qutb's view that turning the living Islamic creed into an abstract theory is a dangerous mistake. Key Takeaway
The objections to calling Islam a 'theory' rest on specific definitions of 'theory' that the author will challenge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Consider the definition of 'theory' assumed by the educational researcher. Could an Islamic educational system be called a 'theory' if we define theory more broadly as a coherent set of principles derived from revelation? Why or why not?
