Understanding Qutb's Nuanced Rejection of 'Theory'
Author refutes misinterpretation of Qutb's view on 'theory'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a blanket rejection of the term 'theory' for Islam and the qualified rejection that occurs only when theory replaces active practice.

Core Idea
Qutb rejects theory only when it paralyzes action, not as a label for Islam's intellectual depth.

Some readers have claimed that Sayyid Qutb rejects the very idea of calling Islam a 'theory.' However, a holistic reading of his works reveals a more nuanced position. This lesson dissects the author's argument that Qutb's critique targets the reduction of Islam to a passive cognitive framework, not the term itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common misunderstanding
Note the initial claim that some understand Qutb's texts as a blanket rejection of the term 'theory' for Islam. The author challenges this reading.
Common misunderstanding: Qutb opposes any theoretical framing of Islam.
2
Extract Qutb's actual critique from the passage
Locate where the author clarifies that Qutb rejects only 'surrender and defeat before Western theories that paralyze the Islamic creed' and 'make it merely a mental cognitive theory.'
3
Find the key qualifying phrase
The author explicitly states: 'Qutb does not take a strict position in rejecting the idea of theory in principle, but he rejects it only when it becomes a substitute for action.' Underline this as the core nuance.
4
Apply the distinction to real texts
Imagine you encounter a passage where Qutb criticizes 'theory.' Determine whether he is attacking the label or the passive mindset. Use the principle that he condemns theory only when it replaces practical faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مناقشة آراء المتحفظين

الخطأ والصواب

إن الأستاذ سيد قطب وإن كان باحثاً يجري عليه ما يجري عليهم من الخطأ والصواب، بيد أنه باحث تتسم نظرته بالعمق، وحجته بالقوة في محمل منهجه؛ ولذلك فإن فكره خليق بالنقاش، وفق منهج كلّي، يتعامل مع ميراثه باعتباره وحدة موضوعية لا تقبل التجزؤ. ومن هذا المنطلق فإن قدراً من الإيمان بالنصوص التي أوردها سيّد في هذه الجزئية سيظهر نتيجة مختلفة عن ذلك الاستنتاج الظاهري للنصوص التي تم إيرادها فيما مضى، وفهم منها بعضهم موقفاً رافضاً. إن النصوص السابقة لا ترفض سوى الاستسلام والانهزام أمام النظريات الغربية التي تشلُ العقيدة الإسلامية عن فاعليتها السلوكية والحركية، وتجعل منها مجرد نظرية معرفية ذهنية فحسب ولقد جاء في معرض نقده ما يؤكد هذا المعنى على وجه قاطع، إذ قال في ظلال قوله تعالى: ﴿وَقُرْآنَا فَرَقْناهُ لِتَقْرَأَهُ عَلَى النَّاسِ عَلَى مُكْثٍ وَنَزَّلْنَاهُ تَنزِيلاً ﴾ [الإسراء: ١٠٦/١٧]. ((فالرفق مقصود والمكـث مقصود كذلك، ليتم البناء التكويني المؤلف من عقيدة في صورة منظمة حيّة (لا) في (صورة) نظرية معرفية)).

الجماعة

وعقب نقده لهذا المعنى قال: ولكن الله - سبحانه - كان يريد أمراً آخر، كان يريد منهجاً متعيناً متفرداً. كان يريد بناء الحركة في وقت واحد. كان يريد أن يبني الجماعة والحركة كان يريد أن تكون العقيدة هي واقع الفعلي، وأن يكون واقع الجماعة الحركي الفعلي في صورة الحقيقة. ولا يتشدد سيد قطب في رفض فكرة النظرية من حيث المبدأ، لكنه يرفضها فقط حين تكون بديلا عن الفاعلية يقول: وهي أي العقيدة الإسلامية في صورتها هذه تشغل من القلوب والعقول ومن الحياة أيضاً مساحة أضخم وأوسع وأعمق مما تشغله (النظرية) وتشمل فيما تشمل مساحة النظرية ومادتها ولكنها لا تقتصر عليها.
Discussion of the views of the cautious ones

Error and correctness

Indeed, Sayyid Qutb, although he is a researcher subject to what researchers are subject to in terms of error and correctness, yet he is a researcher whose vision is characterized by depth and whose argument is strong in the course of his methodology; therefore, his thought is worthy of discussion, according to a holistic methodology that deals with his legacy as an objective unit that does not accept fragmentation. From this standpoint, a certain degree of faith in the texts that Sayyid presented in this particular issue will yield a different result from that apparent conclusion of the texts that were presented previously, from which some understood a rejecting stance. Indeed, the previous texts reject only surrender and defeat before Western theories that paralyze the Islamic creed from its behavioral and dynamic effectiveness, and turn it into merely a mental cognitive theory. And in the context of his critique, that which confirms this meaning in a decisive manner has come, as he said in the shadow of the Almighty's saying: 'And it is a Qur'an which We have separated [verses] that you may recite it to the people with delay and We have sent it down gradually.' [Al-Isra 17:106]. 'Deliberation is intended, and leisurely pace is also intended, so that the formative structure composed of a creed in a living organized form (and not) in the form of a cognitive theory is accomplished.'

The Community

And after his critique of this meaning, he said: 'But Allah - Glorified be He - wanted something else; He wanted a specific, unique methodology. He wanted to build movement at the same time. He wanted to build the community and the movement. He wanted the creed to be the actual reality, and for the actual dynamic reality of the community to be in the form of truth.' And Sayyid Qutb does not take a strict position in rejecting the idea of theory in principle, but he rejects it only when it becomes a substitute for action. He says: 'And it (i.e., the Islamic creed in this form) occupies from hearts and minds and from life as well a space greater, wider, and deeper than what (theory) occupies, and it includes, among what it includes, the scope and material of theory, but it is not limited to it.'
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a critical discussion of the view that the term 'theory' should not be applied to Islam. The author begins by acknowledging that Sayyid Qutb, like all researchers, is subject to error and correctness, but emphasizes the depth and strength of Qutb's arguments. The author then argues that Qutb's statements, when read holistically, do not reject the concept of theory per se, but only reject the submissive acceptance of Western theories that paralyze the Islamic creed's practical and dynamic effectiveness, reducing it to a mere cognitive theory. To support this, the author quotes Qutb's commentary on Quran 17:106, where Qutb emphasizes that the Quran's gradual revelation was intended to build a living creed, not a theoretical framework. The passage further explains that Qutb's goal was to build a community and a movement, making the creed an actual reality. Crucially, the author clarifies that Qutb does not strictly reject the idea of theory in principle; he only rejects it when it becomes a substitute for active engagement. The Islamic creed, according to Qutb, encompasses and surpasses theory in scope and depth.

Sayyid Qutb's critique of 'theory' is not a rejection of intellectual frameworks but a call to ensure that theory serves practice, not replaces it.

Sayyid Qutb's Critique of Purely Cognitive Theory
Author defends a practical-directive theory for Islamic education against Qutb's critique of pure cognitive theory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between predictive-scientific and practical-directive theories and explain why Sayyid Qutb's critique does not reject all theory, only theory detached from practice.

Core Idea
Theory in Islam integrates creed, behavior, and action—it is not merely cognitive.

Sayyid Qutb is often misunderstood as rejecting the concept of 'theory' altogether. In this passage, the author clarifies that Qutb only rejects Western theories that paralyze the Islamic creed's dynamic role, reducing it to a mental exercise. The author then expands on the dual meaning of 'theory'—as predictive-scientific or practical-directive—to show that Islamic educational theory is the latter, encompassing both principles and application.

Guided Path
1
Identify Qutb's target
Read the passage and locate where Qutb criticizes 'theory'. Note that he does not reject theory per se, but only when it becomes a substitute for effectiveness and separates creed from behavior.
Look for phrases like 'mere cognitive mental theory' and 'intellectual luxury'.
2
Extract the two meanings of theory
The author mentions that theory is divided into two: predictive-scientific (تنبئية علمية) and practical-directive (توجيهية عملية). Identify which one the author considers appropriate for Islamic education.
The practical-directive theory is based on knowledge (not natural science) and guides actions.
3
Apply the distinction to Qutb's critique
Explain how Qutb's rejection targets only the cognitive, detached form of theory, not the practical-directive one. The Islamic creed, according to Qutb, includes the space and matter of theory but is not limited to it.
The author uses Qutb's commentary on Quran 17:106 to support this.

((فالرفق مقصود والمكـث مقصود كذلك، ليتم البناء التكويني المؤلف من عقيدة في صورة منظمة حيّة (لا) في (صورة) نظرية معرفية)). وعقب نقده لهذا المعنى قال: ولكن الله - سبحانه - كان يريد أمراً آخر، كان يريد منهجاً متعيناً متفرداً. كان يريد بناء الحركة في وقت واحد. كان يريد أن يبني الجماعة ،والحركة كان يريد أن تكون العقيدة هي واقع الفعلي، وأن يكون واقع الجماعة الحركي الفعلي في صورة الحقيقة)). ولا يتشدد سيد قطب في رفض فكرة النظرية من حيث المبدأ، لكنه يرفضها فقط حين تكون بديلا عن الفاعلية يقول: وهي أي) العقيدة الإسلامية في صورتها هذه تشغل من القلوب والعقول ومن الحياة أيضاً مساحة أضخم وأوسع وأعمق مما تشغله (النظرية) وتشمل فيما تشمل مساحة النظرية ومادتها ولكنها لا تقتصر عليها)). إذن فإن نقد سيّد منصب عليها حين تفصل بين العقيدة والسلوك، أو بين النظرية والتطبيق باسم (نظرية المعرفة) مما يعد ترفاً فكرياً أكثر منه معرفة محردة. ولما كان السلوك ركناً ركيناً في عملية التربية، بل إنه أول لازم من لوازمها بصورة بدهية لا تكلف فيها ولا تعقيد، فإن نقد اصطلاح (نظرية المعرفة في القرآن الكريم) استناداً إلى وقوع هذا الانشطار، أو التحسس من الوقوع فيه، يصبح غير ذي مضمون هنا بوصف التطبيقات التربوية لهذه النظرية أحد العناصر الرئيسة في الدراسة الحالية. ومن هنا فيمكن القول: إن النظرية - في هذه الدراسة - ستشمل - بإذن الله تعالى - مساحة النظرية ومادتها دون أن تقتصر عليها، إذ ستنتقل إلى انعكاساتها المباشرة تلقائياً. وأما رفض أحد الباحثين وصف التربية الإسلامية بالنظرية بحجة أن النظرية إنما هي مجموع المبادئ المترابطة التي توجّه العمليات التربوية، وتحكم الممارسات التعليمية))؛ فإن أكبر خلل منهجي وقع فيه صاحب هذا الاحتجاج أنه انتقى أحد معنيين رئيسين للنظرية وافترضه الصواب وحده، ومن ثم راح يوجه انتقاداته للمصطلح. إن صاحب هذا الرأي لم يزد عن أن تبنى وجهة فريق من الباحثين الغربيين الذين رأوا أن النظرية التربوية هي مجموعة المبادئ المترابطة.. إلخ). ومن بينهم مور (More) الذي سبق رأيه عند الحديث عن معاني النظرية. وقد قسمها إلى :قسمين أحدهما تنبئية علمية والآخر توجيهية عملية. فليس معنى وإذا تأكد لنا أن النظرية التربوية الإسلامية المنشودة ليست تنبئية تفسيرية ذلك أنها توجيهية عملية بإطلاق وإن كانت النظرية التربوية العملية أقرب إلى المفهوم الصحيح للتربية لأنها ترى المعرفة وليس العلم الطبيعي أساساً لمحتواها... وهذا يؤهل النظرية التربوية لتكون نظرية عملية توجه
Therefore, his thought is worthy of discussion, according to a comprehensive methodology, dealing with his legacy as an objective unit that cannot be fragmented. From this perspective, a degree of faith in the texts that Sayyid cited in this part will show a result different from the apparent conclusion of the texts previously cited, from which some understood a rejecting stance. The previous texts only reject submission and defeat before Western theories that paralyze the Islamic creed from its behavioral and dynamic effectiveness, and make it merely a cognitive mental theory. And in the context of his critique, what confirms this meaning definitively came, as he said in the shadows of His statement: "And a Qur'an which We have divided [into parts]..." [al-Isra 17:106]: "Gentleness is intended, and slowness is also intended, so that the formative building composed of a creed in a living organized form (not) in a (form of) cognitive theory." And following his critique of this meaning, he said: "But Allah - the Exalted - wanted something else; He wanted a specific unique methodology. He wanted to build the movement at the same time. He wanted to build the community and the movement. He wanted the creed to be the actual reality, and the actual dynamic reality of the community to be in the form of truth." And Sayyid Qutb is not strict in rejecting the idea of theory in principle, but he only rejects it when it becomes a substitute for effectiveness. He says: "And (the Islamic creed) in this form occupies from hearts and minds and from life as well a larger, wider, and deeper space than what (theory) occupies, and includes among its scope the space and matter of theory but is not limited to it." So, then, Sayyid's critique is directed at it when it separates between creed and behavior, or between theory and application under the name "theory of knowledge," which is more intellectual luxury than pure knowledge. Since behavior is a firm pillar in the process of education, indeed it is the first necessary condition of its necessities in an obvious manner without artifice or complexity, then criticizing the term "theory of knowledge in the Noble Qur'an" based on the occurrence of this split, or wariness of falling into it, becomes meaningless here, describing the educational applications of this theory as one of the main elements in the current study. Hence it can be said: The theory - in this study - will include - by the permission of Allah - the space and matter of theory without being limited to it, as it will move to its direct reflections automatically. As for one researcher's rejection of describing Islamic education as a theory on the pretext that theory is only a set of interrelated principles that guide educational processes and govern teaching practices, the greatest methodological flaw committed by the proponent of this objection is that he selected one of two main meanings of theory and assumed it alone to be correct, and then began directing his criticisms at the term. This opinion holder did nothing but adopt the viewpoint of a group of Western researchers who saw that educational theory is a set of interrelated principles... etc. Among them is More, whose opinion was mentioned earlier when discussing the meanings of theory. He divided it into two parts: one predictive scientific and the other practical directive. So it is not the meaning... And if it is confirmed to us that the desired Islamic educational theory is not predictive-interpretive, but rather it is practical-directive absolutely, even if practical educational theory is closer to the correct concept of education because it sees knowledge and not natural science as the basis of its content... This qualifies the educational theory to be a practical theory that directs.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a critical discussion of how to define 'theory' (النظرية) in the context of Islamic education, building on Sayyid Qutb's views. The author begins by asserting that Sayyid Qutb's thought must be approached holistically. Previous texts might have been misinterpreted as rejecting all theories, but the author clarifies that they only reject Western theories that paralyze the Islamic creed's active role, reducing it to a mere cognitive theory. The author then presents Qutb's commentary on Quran 17:106 to show that the Quran intends a living, organized creed, not a cognitive theory. Qutb insists that Allah wanted a unique methodology that builds movement and community simultaneously, making the creed an actual reality. The author notes that Qutb does not reject theory per se, only when it replaces practical effectiveness. The Islamic creed encompasses theory but goes beyond it. Thus, Qutb's critique targets any separation between creed and behavior, or between theory and application, calling it intellectual luxury. Since behavior is essential to education, the author argues that criticizing the term 'theory of knowledge in the Quran' based on feared separation is unfounded in this study, because the study will include both the space of theory and its practical applications. The author then addresses another researcher's objection to calling Islamic education a theory, arguing that this researcher wrongly assumed only one meaning of theory (as a set of principles). The author points out that theory has two main meanings: predictive-scientific and practical-directive. The desired Islamic educational theory is practical-directive, based on knowledge (not natural science), making it a practical guiding theory. The passage defends a broader, inclusive definition of theory that integrates theory and practice.

Key Terms
نظرية (nazariyya): In this passage, 'theory' is discussed as having two meanings: a predictive-scientific theory (تنبئية علمية) and a practical-directive theory (توجيهية عملية). The author argues that Islamic educational theory is the latter, not merely a set of principles but also encompassing practical application. [Note: In classical Islamic logic (mantiq), 'nazariyya' often means theoretical knowledge as opposed to practical. Here, the term is used in a modern educational context with a specific bifurcation.]
تربية إسلامية (tarbiya islamiyya): Islamic education, understood as a practical-directive theory that integrates creed, behavior, and action, not merely cognitive knowledge. [Note: No significant shift; this term is stable in modern usage.]

Distinguishing Revelation from Human Theory
Critique of conflating revelation and human theory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical error of conflating definitive and speculative religious texts, and distinguish between infallible revelation and fallible human theorizing.

Core Idea
Mixing infallible revelation with fallible human theory is an epistemological category error.

In this passage, the author critiques a scholar who rejects the term 'theory' for Islamic education by pointing out that the scholar fails to distinguish between texts of definitive indication (qat'i al-dalala) and speculative indication (zanni al-dalala). This conflation leads to a false equivalence between divine revelation and human ijtihad. As students of Islamic logic, you will learn to spot such conflations and appreciate the need for precise terminology in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the critique target and his position
The author is responding to a scholar who objects to calling Islamic education a 'theory' because theory is unstable, while revelation is stable. Identify what the target scholar claims and why he objects.
The target scholar sees any use of 'theory' as undermining the stability of revelation.
2
Extract the author's key distinction
The author points out that the target scholar ignores the difference between qat'i (definitive) and zanni (speculative) texts. All texts are sacred, but not all are equally clear or definitive in meaning.
This distinction is standard in usul al-fiqh.
3
Analyze the logical error of conflation
By treating all texts as equally definitive, the target scholar mixes revelation (infallible) with human interpretation (fallible). The author argues that this is a category error: revelation is absolute, while theory (ijtihad) is human reasoning about revelation.
The error leads to rejecting any human formulation as contradictory to revelation.
4
Apply the correction: separate source from formulation
The author clarifies that the stability lies in revealed principles, not in the human theoretical framework. The human element (ijtihad) is fallible and revisable. Distinguish between the source (wahy) and the product (nazariyya).
This lesson teaches you to avoid conflating the divine with the human in any Islamic discipline.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما استغراب الباحث ذاته من المناداة بثبات النظرية التربوية الإسلامية مع العلم بأن النظرية غير ثابتة بل قابلة للرفض، فسيزول سرّ هذا الاستغراب إذا ما وقفنا عند فهمه للنص القرآني والنبوي بصورة عامة. إذ إنه يتجاهل التفريق بين نص صريح قطعي الدلالة، وبين ظني حمال أوجه، بوصف الجميع نصوصاً مقدسة وكفى. ولذلك نراه ينتقد بعض الباحثين (۳) حينما يسعون لبلورة النظرية التربوية الإسلامية)، والاستناد إلى القرآن والسنة، ثم الدراسات التاريخية والتربوية لآراء العلماء المسلمين ومعطيات البحوث العلمية الصحيحة غير المتعارضة مع العقيدة الإسلامية، كمصادر تختلف في أهميتها وأولويات الأخذ منها. إنه يعد ذلك خلطاً للينابيع إذ كيف يكون الكتاب والسنة مساويين للتراث الإسلامي وسواه من المصادر، أوليس في ذلك جمع بين الوحي المعصوم والاجتهاد غير المعصوم؟ أو الإسلام والميراث الإسلامي؟ إن الخطورة - في نظره - تكمن في الجمع بين أصول ربانية مطلقة وليست نظرية، وبين نظرية تقبل الخطأ والصواب والصدق والكذب والحق والباطل. ويمضي في طرح وجهته متسائلاً: إذا قيل المبادئ ثابتة في النظرية التربوية الإسلامية المقترحة فكيف تكون ثابتة، لأن مصدرها الوحي وتكون نظرية في الوقت نفسه؟!(۳). إذن فإن حمله للنصوص القرآنية والنبوية على حال واحدة من حيث دلالتها، وعدم تفريقه بين مسألة القطعية في الورود، والقطعية في الدلالة من وراء رفضه للمصطلح والمعلوم أن نصوص السنة تشمل ما هو قطعي في الورود والدلالة أو ما هو ظنيها، والقرآن يشترك مع صحيح السنة في قدر لا يستهان بـه مـن النصوص ظنية الدلالة جميع ذلك مما لم يراعه الباحث، بل تجاوزه إلى تحميل دعاة بناء نظرية تربوية إسلامية)، الخلط في الينابيع بين الوحي المعصوم والاجتهاد القابل للنقد، العرضة للرد والخلط الحقيقي إنما هو في فهمه، إذ لم يفرق بين النظرية وبين مصادرها بحيث أغفل دور الإنسان في التعامل مع المصادر البلورة النظرية. ولعله من الطّريف هنا الإشارة إلى أن أحد الباحثين تلك عنه الذين أخذ عليهم الباحث وصفهم للتربية الإسلامية بالنظرية باحث عرف الالتزام بنصوص الوحي في كتاباته ومنهجه عموماً، وعُرف أيضاً بتشدده في استخدام بعض المصطلحات كوصف التربية الإسلامية بـ(الفلسفة) مثلاً، ومع ذلك فإن مأخذ الباحث - صاحب الرد - عليه كان في استخدامه (مصطلح النظرية لوصف التربية الإسلامية بها والسؤال إذن كيف يختلف باحث مسلم ينهل من معين نصوص الكتاب والسنة مع زميله الذي ينهل من المعين ذاته؟ الحق أن ذلك يعود - قبل أي سبب آخر - إلى عدم تحرير النزاع في مصطلحي الوحي والنظرية على نحو كاف. وإذا كنا قد عرفنا طبيعة نصوص الوحي فيما سبق فإن مصلح (نظرية) هو الآخر بحاجة إلى تحرير محل النزاع فيه. وفي سبيل هذا أقول: لعله من غير المقبول ولا المعقول أن يتبادر إلى الذهن أن باحثاً مسلماً ملتزماً - بالتربية الإسلامية أو سواها – لا يفرق عن قصد بين نصوص الكتاب وصحيح السنة وبين الاجتهاد الذي يساوي معنى النظرية بجامع الأخذ والعطاء، والقبول والرفض، واحتمال الوقوع في الخطأ أو الباطل كذلك. إن الاجتهاد أو النظرية – بحسب اصطلاح الدراسة – هو الذي يجري عليه كل تلك العوارض، أي إن الاجتهاد نتاج لتفاعل العقل مع النص، وليس مدخلاً مع النص ابتداء كمقدمة له تتساوى في نتيجتها مع مراد النص تماماً. وبتعبير آخر
As for the researcher's own puzzlement about the call for the stability of Islamic educational theory, knowing that theory is not stable but subject to rejection, the secret of this puzzlement will disappear if we pause at his understanding of the Quranic and Prophetic text in general. For he ignores the distinction between a clear text of definitive indication and a speculative text bearing multiple interpretations, describing all as sacred texts and that's enough. Therefore we see him criticizing some researchers (3) when they seek to crystallize Islamic educational theory, relying on the Quran and Sunnah, then historical and educational studies of the opinions of Muslim scholars and data from sound scientific research not conflicting with Islamic creed, as sources that differ in their importance and priority. He considers that a mixing of sources: how can the Book and Sunnah be equal to Islamic heritage and other sources? Is that not combining infallible revelation with non-infallible ijtihad? Or Islam and Islamic inheritance? The danger - in his view - lies in combining absolute divine principles that are not theoretical, with a theory that accepts error and correctness, truth and falsehood, right and wrong. He continues presenting his viewpoint, asking: if it is said that the principles are fixed in the proposed Islamic educational theory, how can they be fixed because their source is revelation and yet they are theoretical at the same time?!(3). So his treatment of Quranic and Prophetic texts as one in terms of their indication, and his failure to distinguish between the issue of definitiveness in transmission and definitiveness in meaning, is behind his rejection of the term. It is known that the texts of the Sunnah include what is definitive in transmission and indication or what is speculative in both, and the Quran shares with the authentic Sunnah a not insignificant amount of texts of speculative indication. All of that the researcher did not take into account; rather he went further to accuse the proponents of building an Islamic educational theory of mixing in sources between infallible revelation and ijtihad subject to criticism and liable to rejection. The real confusion is in his understanding, for he did not distinguish between the theory and its sources, such that he overlooked the role of the human being in dealing with the sources for crystallizing the theory. Perhaps it is interesting here to point out that one of the researchers whom he criticized for describing Islamic education as theory is a researcher known for commitment to the texts of revelation in his writings and methodology in general, and also known for his strictness in using some terms such as describing Islamic education as 'philosophy' for example. Nevertheless, the criticism of the researcher - the respondent - against him was in his use of the term 'theory' to describe Islamic education. So the question is: how does a Muslim researcher who draws from the same source of the texts of the Book and Sunnah differ from his colleague who draws from the same source? The truth is that this goes back - before any other reason - to insufficient clarification of the dispute regarding the terms 'revelation' and 'theory'. And if we have known the nature of the texts of revelation previously, the term 'theory' also needs clarification of the point of dispute. For this purpose, I say: it is perhaps unacceptable and unreasonable that it should come to mind that a committed Muslim researcher - in Islamic education or otherwise - deliberately does not distinguish between the texts of the Book and authentic Sunnah and between ijtihad, which is equivalent to the meaning of theory, given the common features of give and take, acceptance and rejection, and the possibility of falling into error or falsehood as well. Indeed, ijtihad or theory - according to the study's terminology - is what incurs all those attributes, meaning ijtihad is the product of the interaction of the mind with the text, and not an input with the text from the beginning as a premise whose result is completely equal to the intended meaning of the text. In other words...
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of a scholar who opposes using the term 'theory' for Islamic education. The author argues that the scholar's confusion stems from equating all religious texts as equally definitive, ignoring the distinction between texts of definitive indication and speculative indication. The author points out that revelation is infallible while human theorizing (ijtihad) is fallible, and mixing them leads to epistemological chaos. The critique follows the scholar's own reasoning: he claims that theory is inherently unstable, so how can an Islamic theory be stable? The author responds that the stability lies in the revealed principles, not in the human formulation. The author further illustrates the confusion by noting that even a strict proponent of revelation used the term 'theory', highlighting the need to clarify the concepts of 'wahy' and 'nazariyya'. Finally, the author defines ijtihad/nazariyya as the product of the mind interacting with the text, not as a substitute for the text itself.

Key Terms
وحي
نظرية
اجتهاد
قطع الدلالة
ظني الدلالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He prefers the term 'philosophy' over 'theory'.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between qat'i and zanni texts is essential to avoid conflating divine revelation with human ijtihad, preserving both the authority of revelation and the legitimacy of human theorizing.

Critique of Inconsistency in Applying 'Theory' to Islamic Education
Author critiques a researcher's inconsistent use of 'theory'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical inconsistency in a researcher's argument about applying the term 'theory' to Islamic education.

Core Idea
Terminological inconsistency undermines the credibility of an academic argument.

In this passage, the author critiques a researcher who claims that the term 'theory' should not be applied to Islam and Islamic education, yet his own study title and content explicitly use the term. This contradiction reveals a lack of intellectual rigor. By analyzing this critique, you will learn to detect similar inconsistencies in academic arguments about Islamic disciplines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the researcher's explicit position
Find in the passage where the researcher states that it is not permissible to apply the term 'theory' to Islam or Islamic education. Note the hesitation and confusion mentioned.
The author notes the researcher's 'dry admonition' concluding impermissibility.
2
Examine the researcher's actual practice
Look at how the researcher uses the term 'theory' in his own work: the study is titled 'The Educational Theory in Islam' and he describes it as a reflection of Islamic theory. Quote his own words.
The author quotes the researcher: 'The educational theory in Islam is based on these fundamental concepts...'
3
Assess the author's critique
Understand why the author finds this contradictory. The researcher's practice contradicts his stated position. Evaluate whether the author's criticism is valid.
The author questions how one can ask if 'theory' applies after using it throughout the study.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والآن فإن السؤال المنطقي هنا أيهما الصواب: مصطلح النظرية أم التصور ؟! إن إيراد هذا النموذج الرافض لاستخدام مصطلح (التصور) لا يعني بالنسبة لهذه الدراسة سوى التدليل على أن مسألة المصطلحات ما تزال إحدى الإشكالات التي تنتظر المعالجة الجادة، لنخرج من نطاق العاطفة والتقليد غالباً إلى روح الباحث وعمق نظر الناقد. ولكن ذلك لا يغير من سلامة استخدام مصطلح (نظرية) على النحو السالف شيئاً يذكر.
وبعد هذا العرض والنقاش فقد يكون من تمام الموضوعية عدم إغفال ما قد يبدو حجة للباحث الذي شايع الباحث السابق - مع تردد وتلكؤ - في تجنب وصف التربية الإسلامية بـ (النظرية).
وأشير إلى أن الشبهات التي ترد عند هذا الباحث أو ذاك لا تخرج في مضمونها عما سبق عرضه ومناقشته. بيد أن المثير في طرح هذه الوجهة هو الاستدراك أو ما يشبهه الذي تخلل ثنايا دراسة هذا الباحث في مسألة جواز إطلاق مصطلح النظرية على الإسلام عموماً، والتربية الإسلامية بوجه خاص. ونقطة الإثارة حقاً هي في هذه الموعظة اليابسة التي خلصت إلى عدم الجواز، مع أن عنوان دراسته هو النظرية التربوية في الإسلام، ثم قرر أن النظرية التربوية في الإسلام هي انعكاس للنظرية الإسلامية.. وبعد أن ساق أساليب النظرية وخصائصها نص عليها في غير موضع في دراسته مقرونة بالتربية الإسلامية، ومن ذلك قوله: ((والنظرية التربوية في الإسلام تستند إلى هذه المفاهيم والمسلمات الأساسية. فغاية النظرية التربوية في الإسلام هي تحقيق هذه المفاهيم والمسلمات والإجابات الكبرى في الإنسان والمجتمع))). أبعد ذلك يصح أن يطرح هذا التساؤل: هل يصح لنا أن نطلق على الإسلام مصطلح نظرية ..؟ وأغرب منه أن يجيب بالنفي المصحوب بقدر من التلكؤ والاضطراب، مما يبعث على الاستغراب والاستنكار معاً، وقد كان في غنى عن ذلك كله.
And now, the logical question here is: which is correct: the term 'theory' or 'concept'? The mention of this model that rejects the use of the term 'concept' does not mean for this study anything other than demonstrating that the issue of terminology is still one of the problems awaiting serious treatment, so that we may emerge from the realm of emotion and imitation often to the spirit of the researcher and the depth of the critic's view. But that does not change the soundness of using the term 'theory' in the aforementioned manner in the least. After this presentation and discussion, it may be a matter of objectivity not to overlook what might appear as an argument for the researcher who followed the previous researcher—with hesitation and reluctance—in avoiding describing Islamic education as a 'theory'. I point out that the doubts that arise from this or that researcher do not deviate in their content from what was previously presented and discussed. However, what is provocative in presenting this perspective is the correction or something similar that permeated the folds of this researcher's study on the issue of the permissibility of applying the term 'theory' to Islam in general, and Islamic education in particular. The truly exciting point is in this dry admonition that concluded with impermissibility, despite the fact that the title of his study is 'The Educational Theory in Islam', and then he decided that the educational theory in Islam is a reflection of the Islamic theory. After he mentioned the methods of the theory and its characteristics, which he stated in more than one place in his study associated with Islamic education, including his statement: 'The educational theory in Islam is based on these fundamental concepts and premises. So the goal of the educational theory in Islam is to realize these concepts, premises, and major answers in man and society.' After that, is it valid to raise this question: Is it valid for us to apply the term 'theory' to Islam? And stranger than that is that he answers in the negative accompanied by a degree of hesitation and confusion, which causes both amazement and disapproval, and he was in no need of all that.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on a researcher who inconsistently rejects the use of the term 'theory' for Islam and Islamic education. The author begins by stating that the logical question is whether 'theory' or 'concept' is the correct term. He then explains that presenting a model that rejects 'concept' serves only to highlight the ongoing problem of terminology. He defends the use of 'theory' as sound. Next, he addresses a researcher who, with hesitation, avoids calling Islamic education a 'theory'. The author points out that such doubts have already been discussed. The provocative aspect is the researcher's correction that concludes impermissibility, even though his own study is titled 'The Educational Theory in Islam' and he describes it as a reflection of the Islamic theory. The author quotes the researcher stating that the educational theory in Islam is based on fundamental concepts and aims to realize them. The author then questions how one can ask whether 'theory' can be applied to Islam, and finds it even stranger that the answer is a reluctant no, calling it astonishing and objectionable. The critique highlights the inconsistency and lack of intellectual rigor.

Key Terms
نظرية (nazariyya): A systematic framework of concepts and principles; here applied to Islam and Islamic education as a comprehensive theoretical system. [Note: No significant shift — the term is used consistently in modern Islamic discourse.]
تصور (tasawwur): A concept or mental representation; here contrasted with 'theory' as the basis for understanding. [Note: In classical mantiq, tasawwur is a simple concept; here it is used more broadly.]
تربية إسلامية (tarbiya islamiyya): Islamic education; the subject under discussion for being described as a theory. [Note: Stable term in modern educational contexts.]

A) The researcher rejects the term 'theory' but uses it in his own study title and content.
B) The researcher provides a strong argument against using 'theory' for Islamic education.
C) The researcher confirms that 'concept' is the correct term.
D) The researcher avoids the topic entirely.

Key Takeaway
Terminological consistency is crucial in academic discourse; a researcher's own practice often reveals the weakness of their theoretical objections.

The Innate Ethics of Knowledge in the Quran
Author introduces ethics of knowledge as innate Quranic principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of the Quranic perspective on the ethics of knowledge as innate principles and explain how they relate to the purpose of knowledge as vicegerency.

Core Idea
Knowledge in the Quran is inherently ethical and tied to human vicegerency.

This lesson introduces the Quranic view that moral values governing knowledge are innate (fitri) in humans. The author argues that these principles exist potentially at birth and become actual through life, and that humans remain aware of them even when violating them—a sign of their innateness. Understanding this foundation helps us see why knowledge and ethics are inseparable in Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about moral values
Find where the author states that moral values are innate rulings or principles. Note the phrase 'أحكاما أو مبادئ فطرية' (rulings or innate principles). This is the central claim.
2
Differentiate potential vs. actual existence
The author says these principles exist 'بالقوة' (potentially) in the mind after birth, then become 'بالفعل' (actual) through life. This is a key distinction: they are not fully developed at birth but require experience.
3
Recognize the evidence of innateness
Look for the sign that these principles are innate: humans are aware of them even when violating them and feel their violation. This awareness is a sign of fitra.
4
Connect knowledge and moral action
The author states that studying ethics requires prior knowledge to choose moral actions. This establishes knowledge as a prerequisite for ethical behaviour.
5
Understand the Quranic source and purpose
The passage concludes that the Quran is the source of these ethics, and the goal of knowledge is to enable humanity to populate the earth as vicegerents (استخلاف). This ties knowledge directly to responsibility.
This step shows the teleological dimension of knowledge in Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول
أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها
أخلاق المعرفة
ينظر القرآن إلى القيم الخلقية في كليتها بوصفها أحكاما أو مبادئ فطرية في الإنسان، توجد - كسائر المبادئ الفطرية - بالقوة في عقل الإنسان بعد ولادته، ثم تكون بالفعل بعد ذلك من خلال حركة الإنسان في الحياة، ولا يعني هذا أن الإنسان ينساق دائما إلى امتثالها بل قد يخالفها، لكنه يبقى عالما بها شاعرًا بمخالفته لها، وهذا من علامات فطريتها.
وتبرز أهمية الحديث عن أخلاق المعرفة كمحدّد معرفي لمضمون العمل الأخلاقي من زاوية أن من الشروط الضرورية لدراسة الأخلاق امتلاك المعرفة مسبقا لاختيار نوعية العمل الأخلاقي.
إن الفرضية القائمة هنا أن القرآن الكريم مصدر هذه الأخلاق، من منطلق أن غاية المعرفة تمكين الإنسان من عمارة الأرض واستخلافها، وفق منهج الله تعالى. وفي ضوء هذا فإن الأخلاق تغدو ضوابط حاكمة في استخدام المعرفة
Chapter One: The Ethics of Knowledge and Its Unity. Ethics of Knowledge. The Quran views moral values in their entirety as innate rulings or principles in man, existing - like other innate principles - potentially in the human mind after his birth, then becoming actual thereafter through man's movement in life. This does not mean that man always inclines to comply with them; rather he may violate them, but he remains aware of them, feeling his violation of them, and this is a sign of their innateness. The importance of speaking about the ethics of knowledge as a cognitive determinant of the content of moral action emerges from the angle that among the necessary conditions for studying ethics is possessing knowledge beforehand to choose the type of moral action. The hypothesis here is that the Noble Quran is the source of these ethics, on the basis that the goal of knowledge is to enable man to populate the earth and be its vicegerent, according to the methodology of God Almighty. In light of this, ethics become governing controls in the use of knowledge.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is the opening of a chapter discussing the ethics of knowledge from a Quranic perspective. It begins by defining moral values as innate (fitri) principles present in humans potentially at birth and actualized through life experience. The author emphasizes that humans are aware of these principles even when they violate them, which is evidence of their innateness. Next, it highlights that to study ethics, one must first have knowledge to choose moral actions. Finally, it asserts that the Quran is the source of these ethics, with the purpose of knowledge being to enable humanity to fulfill the vicegerency of the earth. This sets the foundation for understanding knowledge as inherently tied to moral responsibility.

Key Takeaway
The Quran teaches that moral values governing knowledge are innate in humans, and their purpose is to guide knowledge toward fulfilling the divine mandate of vicegerency.

Quranic Ethics of Knowledge: Unity and Avoiding Desires
Author discusses two Quranic values for knowledge seekers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Quranic ethical principles for knowledge seekers and explain how violating them leads to societal division and injustice.

Core Idea
Knowledge without ethics becomes a weapon of division; the Quran commands unity and warns against desires.

The passage presents knowledge as a double-edged sword. Islamic education takes a constructive stance, bound by ethical controls. The Quran provides two key values: prohibiting doctrinal differences and warning against following desires. In this lesson, we will explore these principles and their implications for knowledge seekers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Quranic principles
Locate the two numbered values in the Arabic text. The first is the prohibition of doctrinal difference (النهي عن الاختلاف العقدي), the second is the warning against following desire (التحذير من اتباع الهوى).
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence for the first principle
Read the verses Al-Imran 3:105, Yunus 10:93, and Al-Baqarah 2:113. They all criticize those who divide after receiving clear knowledge. Yunus 10:93 highlights that the Children of Israel only differed after knowledge had come, showing that knowledge alone does not prevent division.
3
Examine the author's interpretation
The author argues that the loss of ethical goals transforms knowledge from a means of unity into a tool for tearing apart the community. The 'ethical crisis' occurs when each party denies the other's knowledge despite both having access to the same truth.
This parallels the Quranic verse where Jews and Christians deny each other while reciting the Book.
4
Analyze the second principle
Al-Baqarah 2:145 equates following desires after knowledge has come with injustice. The author emphasizes that certain knowledge must subordinate personal whims, otherwise knowledge becomes a source of oppression.
5
Synthesize the overall message
The passage concludes that knowledge without character and proper goals leads to transgression, corruption, and fragmentation. Therefore, knowledge must aim to unify belief and be bound by the etiquette of disagreement.
The author calls for knowledge that serves human welfare and ethical controls.

الباب الثاني: الفصل الأول- أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها حيث إن المعرفة - أي معرفة - سلاح ذو حدين، يمكن استعمالها في التعمير أو التدمير، كما هو الحاصل في التطبيقات التقنية للعلوم والرياضيات مثلاً، فإنها قد أدت إلى اختراع وسائل في الصناعة والزراعة والمواصلات والأقمار الصناعية يمكن أن تسهم إلى حد كبير في بناء الكون وإعماره. كما أدت إلى اختراع أسلحة الدمار الشامل، وبذلك فإنها تسهم أيضاً في تدمير البشرية أو تهديدها على الأقل. والموقف الذي تتبناه التربية الإسلامية هو أنها تربية بانية لا هادمة، تلتزم بالضوابط الأخلاقية في مسيرة الإنسان المعرفية وما يرتبط بها من وسائل وغايات لا تخرج عن نفع الإنسان، ومصالحه المعتبرة. وعلى هذا فقد جاء القرآن الكريم بجملة من القيم ينبغي على طالب المعرفة التحلي بها، ومنها:
١ - النهي عن الاختلاف العقدي:
وذلك أن القرآن الكريم قد نهى - في غير آية - عن مسلك بعض أهل الكتاب، الذين تباينت أحكامهم وتصوراتهم الجملة قضايا الدين عندهم، رغم توافر المعرفة على نحو بين: ﴿وَلا تَكُونُوا كَالَّذِينَ تَفَرَّقُوا وَاخْتَلَفُوا مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا جَاءَهُمُ الْبَيِّنَاتُ وَأُولَئِكَ لَهُمْ عَذابٌ عَظِيمٌ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٠٥/٣]. وَلَقَدْ بَوَّأْنَا بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ مُبَوَّاً صِدْقٍ وَرَزَقْنَاهُمْ مِنَ الطَّيِّبَاتِ فَمَا اختَلَفُوا حَتَّى جَاءَهُمُ الْعِلْمُ [يونس: ٩٣/١٠]. وهذه الآية الأخيرة تشير إلى أن من أخطر الإصابات الذاتية التي يمكن أن تلحق بالنخبة والأمة على حد سواء: انتقال علل التدين التي كانت سبباً في سقوط الأمم السابقة، وانقراضها عندما افتقد العلم أخلاقه وأهدافه الخيرة فتحول من معرفة بالله إلى وسيلة باغية وأصبح سبباً في تمزيق الأمة، وتفريق الدين. وتجلت الأزمة الأخلاقية أبرز ما تكون حين أنكر كل طرف على الآخر معارفه ومعتقداته مع حصول المعرفة لدى الجميع: ﴿وَقَالَتِ الْيَهُودُ لَيْسَتِ النَّصَارَى عَلَى شَيْءٍ وَقَالَتِ النَّصَارَى لَيْسَتِ الْيَهُودُ عَلَى شَيْءٍ وَهُمْ يَتْلُونَ الْكِتابَ كَذَلِكَ قَالَ الَّذِينَ لا يَعْلَمُونَ مِثْلَ قَوْلِهِمْ فَاللَّهُ يَحْكُمُ بَيْنَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ فِيمَا كَانُوا فِيهِ يَخْتَلِفُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ١١٣/٢]. وحقاً فإن العلم من دون توفر الخلق، وتحديد الأهداف والمقاصد سوف ينقلب إلى لون من البغي والظلم والفساد وتفريق الدين، ويكون سبباً للفرقة والتنازع والتآكل بدل أن يكون سببا في الوحدة والتكامل والقوة. وهنا يجب أن تقدم المعارف الهادفة إلى توحيد المعتقد، والملتزمة بآداب الخلاف.
٢ - التحذير من اتباع الهوى
وذلك لأن القرآن قد عدّ اتباع الهوى خاصة في حال توافر المعرفة اليقينية ضرباً من الظلم: ﴿وَلَئِنِ اتَّبَعْتَ أَهْوَاءَهُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا جَاءَكَ مِنَ الْعِلْمِ إِنَّكَ إِذًا لَمِنَ الظَّالِمِينَ﴾ [البقرة: ١٤٥/٢].
Chapter Two: Section One - Ethics of Knowledge and Its Unity. Whereas knowledge - any knowledge - is a double-edged sword, it can be used for construction or destruction, as is the case in technical applications of sciences and mathematics for example, for they have led to the invention of means in industry, agriculture, transportation, and satellites that can contribute greatly to building and developing the universe. They have also led to the invention of weapons of mass destruction, and thus they also contribute to the destruction of humanity or at least threatening it. And the position adopted by Islamic education is that it is a constructive education, not destructive, committed to ethical controls in the human epistemological journey and what is associated with it of means and ends that do not deviate from the benefit of man and his considered interests. And upon this, the Noble Quran has come with a set of values that the seeker of knowledge should adhere to, including: 1 - The prohibition of doctrinal difference: That is because the Noble Quran has prohibited - in more than one verse - the approach of some of the People of the Book, whose judgments and overall perceptions of religious issues differed among themselves, despite the availability of knowledge in a clear manner: {And be not like those who became divided and differed after the clear proofs had come to them. And those will have a great punishment} [Al-Imran 3:105]. {And We had settled the Children of Israel in a secure settlement and provided them with good things. And they did not differ until after knowledge had come to them} [Yunus 10:93]. And this last verse indicates that among the most dangerous self-inflicted harms that can afflict both the elite and the community alike is: the transmission of the ailments of religiosity that were the cause of the fall of previous nations and their extinction when knowledge lost its ethics and benevolent goals, transforming from knowledge of God into a transgressing means and becoming a cause for tearing apart the community and dividing the religion. And the ethical crisis manifested most clearly when each side denied the other's knowledge and beliefs despite the possession of knowledge by all: {And the Jews said, "The Christians are not upon anything," and the Christians said, "The Jews are not upon anything," although they recite the Book. Thus spoke those who do not know like their statement. So Allah will judge between them on the Day of Resurrection concerning that over which they used to differ} [Al-Baqarah 2:113]. Indeed, knowledge without the availability of character and the determination of goals and objectives will turn into a kind of transgression, injustice, corruption, and division of religion, and become a cause for division, discord, and erosion instead of being a cause for unity, integration, and strength. And here, knowledge must be presented that aims at unifying belief and is committed to the etiquette of disagreement. 2 - The warning against following desire: That is because the Quran has considered following desire, especially when certain knowledge is available, as a form of injustice: {And if you follow their desires after what has come to you of knowledge, indeed, you would then be among the wrongdoers} [Al-Baqarah 2:145].
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage introduces the ethics of knowledge from an Islamic perspective, emphasizing that knowledge is neutral but its application can be constructive or destructive. The author contrasts technical advancements (industry, agriculture, satellites) with weapons of mass destruction to illustrate the dual potential. The Islamic educational stance is constructive, bound by ethical guidelines that serve human welfare. The Quran provides values for knowledge seekers, and the author extracts two key principles. First, the prohibition of doctrinal differences: The Quran criticizes those who divide after receiving clear evidence, citing verses condemning factionalism. The author interprets this as a warning that knowledge without ethics leads to societal decay, as seen in past nations. The verse about Jews and Christians denying each other's validity despite having scripture exemplifies how knowledge becomes a tool for division when ethics are absent. The author concludes that knowledge without character and proper goals leads to injustice and fragmentation, so knowledge must aim to unify belief and follow proper disagreement etiquette. Second, the warning against following desire: The Quran equates succumbing to personal whims after gaining certain knowledge with oppression. This highlights that ethical conduct requires subordinating desires to truth.

التربية الإسلامية
الاختلاف العقدي

The Quran's Rejection of Conjectural Knowledge
Author discusses Quranic prohibition of conjecture as basis for knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic verses that forbid relying on conjecture and explain the reasoning behind the prohibition.

Core Idea
The Quran rejects knowledge based on conjecture, no matter how many believe it.

This passage establishes the Quran's epistemological stance: true knowledge cannot be built on conjecture (zann). The author cites two key verses to support this principle: Surah Al-An'am 6:116 warns that following the majority leads to misguidance because they follow only conjecture, and Surah Al-Jathiya 45:24 denies that conjecture constitutes real knowledge. This lesson will help you understand why the Quran demands certainty over popular opinion.

Guided Path
1
Extract the author's claim
Identify the opening statement: the Quran does not give weight to knowledge based on conjecture. What is the general principle?
2
Analyze Al-An'am 6:116
Read the verse and note its warning about following the majority. What is the relationship between majority opinion and conjecture?
The verse equates following the majority with following conjecture.
3
Analyze Al-Jathiya 45:24
This verse denies that those who follow conjecture have any knowledge. How does this reinforce the principle?
4
Synthesize the standard
Combine the two verses: what epistemological standard does the Quran establish?
The standard is that conjecture is not a valid basis for knowledge, regardless of the number of adherents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالنَّهْيُ عَنِ الْمَعْرِفَةِ الظَّنِّيَّةِ (١): وَالْقُرْآنُ لَا يُقِيمُ وَزْنًا لِمَعْرِفَةٍ قَائِمَةٍ عَلَى الظَّنِّ وَالْخَرْصِ مَهْمَا كَانَتْ كَثْرَةُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ بِهَا: ﴿وَإِن تُطِعْ أَكْثَرَ مَنْ فِي الْأَرْضِ يُضِلُّوكَ عَن سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ إِن يَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا الظَّنَّ وَإِنْ هُمْ إِلَّا يَخْرُصُونَ﴾ [الأنعام: ١١٦/٦]. وَنَفْيُ أَيِّ مَعْنًى لِلْمَعْرِفَةِ مَا دَامَ مَبْنَاهَا قَائِمًا عَلَى الظَّنِّ لَا أَكْثَرَ: ﴿... وَمَا لَهُم بِذَلِكَ مِنْ عِلْمٍ إِنْ هُمْ إِلَّا يَظُنُّونَ﴾ [الحانية: ٢٤/٤٥]. وَفِي حَدِيثِ الْقُرْآنِ عَنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ وَرَدَ مَا يُفِيدُ أَنَّ مَعْرِفَتَهُمْ بِالْكِتَابِ لَمْ تَتَجَاوَزِ الْخَوَاطِرَ الْعَابِرَةَ وَالرُّؤَى السَّطْحِيَّةَ الَّتِي ظَاهِرُهَا الْعِلْمُ وَبَاطِنُهَا مِنْ قَبِيلِ الْعَيْبِ وَالْجَهْلِ، وَذَلِكَ مَا يُسَمِّيهِ الْقُرْآنُ (الْأَمَانِيَّ) الَّتِي سَبَبُهَا ظَنُّهُم: ﴿وَمِنْهُمْ أُمِّيُّونَ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ الْكِتَابَ إِلَّا أَمَانِيَّ وَإِنْ هُمْ إِلَّا يَظُنُّونَ﴾ [البقرة: ۷۸/۲]. وَفِي نَهْيِ الْقُرْآنِ عَنِ الظَّنِّ الْمَرْجُوحِ تَرْبِيَةٌ لِلْمُتَعَلِّمِ عَلَى السَّعْيِ نَحْوَ اسْتِخْلَاصِ النَّتَائِجِ الْعِلْمِيَّةِ بِدِقَّةٍ، وَعَدَمِ الرُّكُونِ إِلَى الظَّنِّ الْمُجَرَّدِ، أَو التَّخْمِينِ الْقَائِمِ عَلَى غَيْرِ مَا بَحْثٍ جَادٍّ مُثَابِرٍ يَسْتَقْصِي الْمَوْضُوعَ الْمَبْحُوثَ مِنْ جَوَانِبِهِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ كَيْفَمَا يُخْلَصُ إِلَى النَّتَائِجِ الْيَقِينِيَّةِ.
And the prohibition of conjectural knowledge (1): The Quran does not give weight to knowledge based on conjecture and speculation, however many believers there may be in it: {If you obey most of those on earth, they will mislead you from the way of Allah. They follow nothing but conjecture, and they are only guessing} [Al-An'am 6:116]. And it denies any meaning to knowledge as long as its foundation is based on nothing more than conjecture: {... And they have no knowledge thereof; they follow but conjecture} [Al-Jathiya 45:24]. And in the Quran's account of the People of the Book, there is what indicates that their knowledge of the Book did not exceed passing thoughts and superficial views whose outward appearance is knowledge but whose inner is a kind of defect and ignorance, and that is what the Quran calls 'amanī' (wishes/false hopes) caused by their conjecture: {Among them are unlettered ones who do not know the Book except through wishful thinking, and they are only conjecturing} [Al-Baqara 2:78]. And in the Quran's prohibition of weak conjecture (al-zann al-marjūḥ) is a training for the learner to endeavor toward deriving scientific results accurately, and not to rely on mere conjecture or guesswork based on anything other than serious diligent investigation that thoroughly examines the subject from its various aspects in order to arrive at certain conclusions.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage discusses the Quran's stance on knowledge based on conjecture (zann). The author begins by stating the general principle: the Quran does not value knowledge founded on conjecture, regardless of how many people believe it. He then cites two verses to support this: first, Surah Al-An'am 6:116, which warns that following the majority leads to misguidance because they follow only conjecture; second, Surah Al-Jathiya 45:24, which denies that conjecture constitutes true knowledge. The author then moves to the People of the Book, explaining that their understanding of the scripture was superficial and amounted to mere 'amanī' (wishes or fantasies), as described in Surah Al-Baqara 2:78. This, the author explains, trains the learner to strive for precise, certain knowledge through diligent and thorough investigation, avoiding reliance on mere guesswork or weak conjecture.

الأماني

The Quran rejects knowledge based on conjecture, regardless of how many people hold it.

Superficial Knowledge and Wishful Thinking: The Quran's Critique of the People of the Book
Author discusses Quranic prohibition of conjecture as basis for knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Quranic term 'amānī' and its relationship to conjecture, using Surah Al-Baqara 2:78.

Core Idea
The Quran labels superficial understanding as 'amānī'—wishful thinking rooted in conjecture.

This passage delves into the Quran's critique of the People of the Book, whose knowledge of scripture did not go beyond passing thoughts and superficial views. The Quran calls this 'amānī' (wishful thinking) and attributes it to their reliance on conjecture. This lesson will help you understand how the Quran distinguishes genuine knowledge from mere wishful thinking, and why this distinction is crucial for learners.

Guided Path
1
Identify the group
Find the reference to the 'unlettered' among the People of the Book in the passage. Who are they?
The passage quotes Al-Baqara 2:78 about 'unlettered ones' who do not know the Book except through amānī.
2
Understand 'amānī'
The author explains 'amānī' as wishful thinking or false hopes. How does the verse describe their knowledge?
The verse says they know the Book only through amānī, and they are only conjecturing.
3
Connect to conjecture
What is the cause of their superficial knowledge? The author says it is their conjecture (zann). How does the verse link amānī and zann?
The verse ends with 'and they are only conjecturing', showing that amānī arises from conjecture.
4
Derive the lesson
What should a learner avoid according to this verse? The author concludes that the Quran trains the learner to strive for exact scientific results and not rely on mere conjecture.

And the prohibition of conjectural knowledge (1): The Quran does not give weight to knowledge based on conjecture and speculation, however many believers there may be in it: {If you obey most of those on earth, they will mislead you from the way of Allah. They follow nothing but conjecture, and they are only guessing} [Al-An'am 6:116]. And it denies any meaning to knowledge as long as its foundation is based on nothing more than conjecture: {... And they have no knowledge thereof; they follow but conjecture} [Al-Jathiya 45:24]. And in the Quran's account of the People of the Book, there is what indicates that their knowledge of the Book did not exceed passing thoughts and superficial views whose outward appearance is knowledge but whose inner is a kind of defect and ignorance, and that is what the Quran calls 'amanī' (wishes/false hopes) caused by their conjecture: {Among them are unlettered ones who do not know the Book except through wishful thinking, and they are only conjecturing} [Al-Baqara 2:78]. And in the Quran's prohibition of weak conjecture (al-zann al-marjūḥ) is a training for the learner to endeavor toward deriving scientific results accurately, and not to rely on mere conjecture or guesswork based on anything other than serious diligent investigation that thoroughly examines the subject from its various aspects in order to arrive at certain conclusions.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage discusses the Quran's stance on knowledge based on conjecture (zann). The author begins by stating the general principle: the Quran does not value knowledge founded on conjecture, regardless of how many people believe it. He then cites two verses to support this: first, Surah Al-An'am 6:116, which warns that following the majority leads to misguidance because they follow only conjecture; second, Surah Al-Jathiya 45:24, which denies that conjecture constitutes true knowledge. The author then moves to the People of the Book, explaining that their understanding of the scripture was superficial and amounted to mere 'amanī' (wishes or fantasies), as described in Surah Al-Baqara 2:78. This, the author explains, trains the learner to strive for precise, certain knowledge through diligent and thorough investigation, avoiding reliance on mere guesswork or weak conjecture.

Key Terms
الظن
الأماني

Checkpoint

A) الخرص
B) الأماني
C) الظن المرجوح
D) الخواطر العامرة

Key Takeaway
Conjecture leads to superficial understanding that the Quran labels 'amānī' – wishful thinking, not true knowledge.

2. Identify a modern situation where some Muslims rely on wishful thinking (amānī) rather than solid evidence in understanding a religious matter, and explain how this lesson would critique it.

Warning Against Falsification of Knowledge
Author warns against distorting truth with falsehood using Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Quranic evidence against falsification of knowledge and explain why it is a severe moral crime.

Core Idea
Falsifying knowledge knowingly is a double moral crime that corrupts truth and invites divine warning.

The Quran is not only a source of creed and law but also a guide for the ethics of knowledge. In this lesson, we examine how Allah warns against the deliberate distortion of truth—a crime that undermines the very foundation of Islamic scholarship. Through four Quranic passages, we see the prohibition of mixing truth with falsehood, concealing truth, and forging scripture for worldly gain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibitions
Read Al-Baqarah 2:42 and Aal-e-Imran 3:71. These verses forbid mixing truth with falsehood (talbis) and concealing truth (kitman). List the exact actions prohibited.
2
Recognize the threat and motive
In Al-Baqarah 2:79, Allah condemns those who write false scripture for material gain. Understand that the motive is selfish and the punishment is severe.
3
Understand the double moral crime
Aal-e-Imran 3:78 describes twisting tongues and claiming lies about Allah while knowing the truth. The author notes this is a double crime because it is deliberate and knowledgeable.
4
Trace the consequence of ignoring truth
Read Al-Baqarah 2:101-102. The Israelites abandoned the Torah and followed magic, leading to harm. This shows that ignoring sound knowledge invites corruption.
5
Connect to ethical principle
The author concludes that presenting knowledge purely yields sound outcomes. Reflect on how this principle applies to Islamic scholarship today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الأول- أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها
٦ - التحذير من تزييف المعرفة
ولذلك فقد جاء الخطاب إلى أهل الكتاب محذراً من أي تلبيس متعمد للمعرفة:
﴿وَلَا تَلْبِسُوا الْحَقَّ بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتَكْتُمُوا الْحَقَّ وَأَنتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٤٢/٢]. وخاطبهم بسؤال استنكاري:
يا أَهْلَ الْكِتابِ لِمَ تَلْبِسُونَ الْحَقِّ بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتَكْتُمُونَ الْحَقَّ وَأَنتُمْ
تَعْلَمُونَ [آل عمران: ۷۱/۳].
وتوعدهم حين يعمدون إلى تحريف المعرفة بدوافع منفعية خالصة: فَوَيْلٌ لِلَّذِينَ يَكْتُبُونَ الْكِتابَ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ ثُمَّ يَقُولُونَ هَذَا مِنْ عِنْدِ اللهِ لِيَشْتَرُوا بِهِ ثَمَناً قَلِيلاً فَوَيْلٌ لَهُمْ مِمَّا كَتَبَتْ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَوَيْلٌ لَهُمْ مِمَّا يَكْسِبُونَ
[البقرة: ٧٩/٢].
وعد مسلك التزييف المعرفي عن سابق علم ومعرفة جُرماً أخلاقيًا مضاعفا : وَإِنَّ مِنْهُمْ لَفَرِيقاً يَلْوُونَ أَلْسِنَتَهُمْ بِالْكِتابِ لِتَحْسَبُوهُ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنَ الْكِتابِ وَيَقُولُونَ هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللهِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللهِ وَيَقُولُونَ عَلَى اللهِ الْكَذِبَ وَهُمْ يَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [آل عمران: ۷۸/۳].
وأشار القرآن الكريم إلى أن إقصاء المعرفة السليمة أو تجاهلها يتبعه بالضرورة إحلال المعرفة مصابة بالزيف والفساد، أو ضارة تؤدي إلى الكفر عند تعلمها، أو ممارستها، هذا عدا الوعيد في الآخرة:
﴿وَلَمّا جَاءَهُمْ رَسُولٌ مِنْ عِنْدِ اللهِ مُصَدِّق لِما مَعَهُمْ نَبَدَ فَرِيقٌ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتابَ كِتابَ اللهِ وَراءَ ظُهُورِهِمْ كَأَنهُمْ لا يَعْلَمُونَ، وَاتَّبَعُوا مَا تَتْلُو الشَّيَاطِينُ عَلَى مُلْكِ سُلَيْمانَ وَمَا كَفَرَ سُلَيْمَانُ وَلَكِنَّ الشَّيَاطِينَ كَفَرُوا يُعَلِّمُونَ النّاسَ السِّحْرَ وَمَا أُنْزِلَ عَلَى الْمَلَكَيْنِ بِبَابِلَ هَارُوتَ وَمَارُوتَ وَمَا
يُعَلِّمَانِ مِنْ أَحَدٍ حَتَّى يَقُولا إِنَّمَا نَحْنُ فِتْنَةٌ فَلا تَكْفُرْ فَيَتَعَلَّمُونَ مِنْهُما ما يُفَرِّقُونَ بِهِ بَيْنَ الْمَرْءِ وَزَوْجِهِ وَمَا هُمْ بِضَارِّينَ بِهِ مِنْ أَحَدٍ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ اللهِ ويَتَعَلَّمُونَ ما يَضُرُّهُمْ وَلا يَنْفَعُهُمْ وَلَقَدْ عَلِمُوا لَمَن اشْتَرَاهُ مَا لَهُ فِي الآخِرَةِ
مِنْ خَلاقٍ وَلَبِئْسَ مَا شَرَوْا بِهِ أَنْفُسَهُمْ لَوْ كَانُوا يَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۰۱/۲-۱۰۲]. وحينما يقدم المنهج المعرفة على حقيقتها نقيّة مجردة، فستأتي المخرجات التعليمية والتربوية سليمة معافاة من الأمراض الاجتماعية المتفشية كالغش والخداع والنفاق.
Chapter Two: First Section - Ethics of Knowledge and Its Unity
6 - Warning against falsification of knowledge
Therefore the address came to the People of the Book warning against any deliberate obfuscation of knowledge: "And do not mix the truth with falsehood nor conceal the truth while you know" [Al-Baqarah 2:42]. And He addressed them with a question of disapproval: "O People of the Book, why do you mix the truth with falsehood and conceal the truth while you know?" [Aal-e-Imran 3:71]. And He threatened them when they deliberately distort knowledge out of pure selfish motives: "So woe to those who write the Book with their own hands then say, 'This is from Allah,' to sell it for a small price. Woe to them for what their hands have written and woe to them for what they earn." [Al-Baqarah 2:79]. And He considered the path of deliberate falsification of knowledge, with prior knowledge and awareness, a double moral crime: "And indeed among them is a party who twist their tongues with the Book so that you think it from the Book, but it is not from the Book. And they say, 'It is from Allah,' but it is not from Allah. And they speak lies about Allah while they know." [Aal-e-Imran 3:78]. And the Noble Quran indicated that excluding or ignoring sound knowledge is necessarily followed by the substitution of knowledge afflicted with falsity and corruption, or harmful knowledge that leads to disbelief when learned or practiced, besides the threat in the Hereafter: "And when there came to them a messenger from Allah confirming what was with them, a party of those who were given the Book threw the Book of Allah behind their backs as if they did not know. And they followed what the devils recited over the kingdom of Solomon. And Solomon did not disbelieve, but the devils disbelieved. They teach people magic and that which was sent down to the two angels at Babylon, Harut and Marut. But they did not teach anyone until they said, 'We are only a trial, so do not disbelieve.' And they learn from them that by which they separate a man from his wife. But they cannot harm anyone with it except by permission of Allah. And they learn what harms them and does not benefit them. And they certainly knew that whoever purchased it would have no share in the Hereafter. And how wretched is that for which they sold themselves, if they only knew." [Al-Baqarah 2:101-102]. And when the methodology presents knowledge in its pure, abstract reality, then the educational and pedagogical outcomes will come sound and free from prevalent social diseases such as cheating, deception, and hypocrisy.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is an ethical warning against the falsification of knowledge. The author begins by citing Quranic verses that address the People of the Book, cautioning them against mixing truth with falsehood and concealing truth deliberately (Al-Baqarah 2:42, Aal-e-Imran 3:71). This is a direct prohibition of intellectual dishonesty. The author then highlights the severe threat against those who distort scripture for worldly gain (Al-Baqarah 2:79) and notes that such deliberate falsification constitutes a double moral crime because it is done knowingly (Aal-e-Imran 3:78). The passage further explains that ignoring sound knowledge necessarily leads to the adoption of corrupted or harmful knowledge, citing the story of the Israelites who abandoned the Torah and followed magic (Al-Baqarah 2:101-102). The author concludes that when knowledge is presented truthfully and purely, educational outcomes are sound and free from social ills like cheating and deception. This passage establishes a foundational ethical principle: knowledge must be preserved from distortion, and those who falsify it bear a grave responsibility.

Key Terms
تزييف المعرفة
التلبيس
كتمان المعرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Deliberate falsification of knowledge is a severe sin that destroys the integrity of truth and incurs divine displeasure.

The Ethical Prohibition of Concealing Knowledge
Author warns against concealing knowledge and ties it to ethical responsibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic evidence for the prohibition of concealing knowledge and explain why material benefit alone is an insufficient criterion for ethical judgment.

Core Idea
Concealing knowledge is a grave sin with severe consequences.

This lesson examines a passage that ties the prohibition of concealing knowledge to ethical responsibility. The author uses Quranic verses to establish the severity of the sin and then draws a contemporary lesson: material gain cannot justify concealment; ethics must prevent harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic prohibitions
Locate the two Quranic verses cited. Note that the first (2:42) prohibits mixing truth with falsehood and concealing truth. The second (2:174) threatens those who conceal divine knowledge for worldly gain with fire and punishment.
2
Analyze the threat structure
Examine the consequences listed in 2:174: consuming fire, no divine speech, no purification, and painful punishment. This shows the severity of concealing knowledge.
3
Extract the contemporary application
The author argues that if humanity embraced openness, science and technology would be shared, not monopolized. This connects the ethical ideal to real-world power imbalances.
4
Derive the broader ethical principle
The passage concludes that material benefit alone is not a sufficient criterion for ethical judgment; it must be accompanied by a commitment to avoid harming others.
This is a key epistemological point: utility is not enough; ethics must constrain knowledge-sharing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التحذير من كتمان المعرفة:
ولذلك فقد ورد في سياق النهي عن تزييف المعرفة أو تلبيسها التحذير أيضا
كتمان المعرفة
﴿وَلا تَلْبِسُوا الْحَقَّ بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتَكْتُمُوا الْحَقَّ وَأَنْتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٤٢/٢].
كما توعدهم بالخسران في الآخرة:
إنَّ الَّذِينَ يَكْتُمُونَ ما أَنْزَلَ اللهُ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَيَشْتَرُونَ بِهِ ثَمَناً قَلِيلاً أُولَئِكَ ما يَأْكُلُونَ فِي بُطُونِهِمْ إِلا النّارَ وَلا يُكَلِّمُهُمُ اللَّهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيامَةِ وَلَا يُزَكِّيهِمْ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ أَلِيمٌ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٧٤/٢].
وعندما تستجيب الإنسانية لهذا الخلق ستنعم بخيرات العلم والتقنية التي احتكرها أقوياء الحضارة الغربية هيمنة واستعلاء على شعوب العالم المتخلف. ولعلنا نكون قد أدركنا من تلك الآيات كذلك أن المنفعة المادية ليست وحدها معيارا كافيًا للحكم على صحة المسلك، مالم يصحب ذلك
التزام أخلاقي، يضمن سلامة عدم كون المنفعة مضرة بأطراف أخرى.
Warning against concealing knowledge:
Therefore, in the context of prohibiting the falsification or obfuscation of knowledge, there is also a warning against concealing knowledge: "And do not mix the truth with falsehood nor conceal the truth while you know" [Al-Baqarah 2:42]. And He threatened them with loss in the Hereafter: "Indeed, those who conceal what Allah has sent down of the Book and exchange it for a small price – they consume nothing into their bellies except fire. And Allah will not speak to them on the Day of Resurrection nor purify them, and for them is a painful punishment." [Al-Baqarah 2:174]. And when humanity responds to this character, it will enjoy the blessings of science and technology that the powerful Western civilization has monopolized, dominating and lording over the underdeveloped peoples of the world. And perhaps we have realized from these verses as well that material benefit alone is not a sufficient criterion for judging the correctness of a path, unless it is accompanied by an ethical commitment that ensures that benefit is not harmful to other parties.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage addresses the ethical prohibition of concealing knowledge. The author begins by linking it to the previous warning against falsification: both are condemned together in the Quranic verse Al-Baqarah 2:42. The author then cites a severe threat directed specifically at those who conceal divine knowledge for worldly gain (Al-Baqarah 2:174), warning that such people will face fire in the Hereafter and be deprived of Allah's speech and purification. The passage then draws a contemporary application: if humanity embraces this ethic of openness, it would share the benefits of science and technology instead of allowing powerful civilizations to hoard them. The author concludes with a broader lesson: material benefit is not a sufficient criterion for moral judgment; it must be accompanied by ethical commitment that prevents harm to others. This reinforces the idea that knowledge is a trust that must be disclosed, not concealed for selfish motives.

المنفعة المادية (al-manfa'a al-madiyya)

Key Takeaway
