The Unity of Knowledge (Wahdat al-Ma'rifa)
Author establishes the principle of unity of knowledge in Islamic education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of wahdat al-ma'rifa and describe how it accommodates specialization without creating a religious-secular duality.

Core Idea
All knowledge, cosmic and religious, shares one origin and method in Islam.

In this passage, the author asserts that Islamic education is based on a holistic view of reality, where all fields of knowledge form a single unity. This does not reject specialization but warns against a fatal split between religious and secular domains. Understanding this unity is key to building an authentic Islamic educational system that respects both revealed and empirical sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of unity
Look at the opening sentences: the author grounds the unity in Islam's holistic view of man, universe, and life. Note the parallelism: 'the source is one, the Creator is one, man is one, the universe is one.' This is the foundation.
This is not a theological claim but an epistemological one about the nature of knowledge.
2
Recognize the denial of a fundamental difference
The author explicitly says there is no difference between 'cosmic sciences' (al-ulum al-kawniyya) and 'religious sciences' (al-ulum al-shar'iyya) in terms of knowledge and method (min haythu al-ma'rifa wa al-tariqa fi al-bahth wa al-tafkir). This is a strong claim.
3
Understand the role of specialization
The author acknowledges the practical necessity of specialization due to the expansion of knowledge, but insists that this division is a 'modern necessity' not a negation of unity. The key is that the 'element of unifying bond' must not be forgotten.
The author uses the term 'takamul al-ma'rifa' (integration of knowledge) to describe how unity and specialization coexist.
4
Reflect on historical examples
The author cites Hunayn ibn Ishaq, Ibn Sina, and al-Kindi as examples of specialists who operated within the framework of unity. These scholars mastered both religious and worldly sciences, showing that specialization does not require duality.
Hunayn was a Christian physician, yet he headed the House of Wisdom—showing that knowledge transcends religious identity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الأول - أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها
المعرفة في التربية الإسلامية منبثقة من نظرة الإسلام الكلية إلى الإنسان والكون والحياة. فحقول المعرفة جميعاً وحدة واحدة في نظر التربية الإسلامية، لا فرق بين علوم كونية وأخرى شرعية كمعرفة وطريقة في البحث والتفكير، إذ إن أصلها واحد، والخالق واحد، والإنسان واحد، والكون واحد، فهي تمثل الوحدة الموضوعية في النظرة إلى المعرفة.
خطر الثنائية
إن الحديث عن تكامل المعرفة انطلاقاً من وحدتها لا يعني عدم الاعتراف بالتخصصات فذلك - إن فهم - فلزوم ما لا يلزم إذ إن الضرورة الموضوعية لـم تعد تسوّغ وجود طلاب علم موسوعيين أو أشبه بدوائر معارف عصرهم كمنهج عام. فغدا التقسيم ضرورة عصرية في ظل تشعب المعرفة، وتفرعها المستمر.
إن تقسيم المعرفة يخدم غاية هامة من حيث تمكين المتعلم من التخصص في حقل ما من حقول المعرفة، ولكنه يجب ألا ننسى عنصر الوحدة الجامعة بين نظم التعليم، لأن ذلك يمثل الخطوة الأولى نحو الحنكة والحصافة.
وقديماً عرف تاريخنا وجود متخصصين في إطار وحدة المعرفة كحنين بـن إسحاق الطبيب النصراني (ت: ٢٦٠ هـ) الذي عينه المأمون على بيت الحكمة، وابن سينا صاحب كتاب (القانون في الطب) (ت: ٤٢٨هـ)، والكندي ت: ٢٦٠هـ) و مدار فلسفته الرياضيات والفلسفة الطبيعية)، وغيرهم.
ولذلك فلا مشكل من هذه الناحية، وإنما الخطر المحقق من تخيل نشوب ثنائية لالقاء بين قطبيها كثنائية التعليم الديني والتعليم المدني.
ويذهب أحد الباحثين في استعراض النتائج التي تجسدت فيها تلك الخطورة على النحو التالي:
-۱- أوجد قطاعًا كبيرًا من المثقفين المسلمين، يقتنع بأن الإسلام لا يصلح لبناء نظام تربوي يلائم مقتضيات العصر.
۲ - صاحب ذلك معاملة المثقفين للإسلام كما يعامل الدين في النظام الغربي التربية الدينية في المدارس العامة، على أنه موضوع مدرسي فحسب.
تسبب في وجود لامبالاة من قبل المسلمين بقضية تطوير النظام الإسلامي التقليدي وتحديثه، مما أكد اتهام المستعمر بأن الإسلام لا يصلح - أصلاً - للتطوير والتحديث.
٤ - عَزَلَ علماء الإسلام عن المواقع القيادية - تبعا لذلك – فكريًا واجتماعيا وسياسيا، واستبدلهم بقيادات علمانية في تعليمها ومن ثم مرجعيتها.
استطاع أن يطرح فكرة تكافؤ الثقافات، مما أتاح طرح فكرة القومية بديلا عن الإسلام، فأتت قيادات قومية أمسكت بزمام المؤسسات الجديدة، على حساب غياب المثقف المسلم.
ومن جانب آخر يتجلى خطر هذه الثنائية في كونها لا تقف بفصلها (الديني عن المدني عند حد البناء الخارجي فحسب، بل تتعدى ذلك لتشمل جملة المنهاج وأهدافه، وبذلك تصبح المحصلة الطبيعية لهذا الخلل الواضح وجود نغطين من الشخصية
Chapter Two: The First Chapter - Ethics of Knowledge and its Unity. Knowledge in Islamic education emanates from Islam's holistic view of man, the universe, and life. All fields of knowledge are one unit in the view of Islamic education; there is no difference between cosmic sciences and religious sciences in terms of knowledge and method in research and thinking, because their source is one, the Creator is one, man is one, and the universe is one. Thus it represents the objective unity in the view of knowledge. The Danger of Duality: Discussion of the integration of knowledge based on its unity does not mean non-recognition of specializations—that, if understood, is a logical fallacy because objective necessity no longer justifies encyclopedic students or like encyclopedias of their time as a general method. Thus division became a modern necessity in light of the branching and continuous ramification of knowledge. The division of knowledge serves an important purpose in enabling the learner to specialize in a field of knowledge, but we must not forget the element of unifying bond between educational systems, because that represents the first step towards wisdom and perspicacity. Historically, our history has known specialists within the framework of the unity of knowledge, such as Hunayn ibn Ishaq the Christian physician (d. 260 AH) who was appointed by al-Ma'mun over the House of Wisdom, and Ibn Sina author of The Canon in Medicine (d. 428 AH), and al-Kindi (d. 260 AH) whose school of philosophy was mathematics and natural philosophy, and others. Therefore, there is no problem from this perspective; the real danger is from imagining the outbreak of a dualistic dichotomy between its two poles, such as the duality of religious education and secular education. One researcher, in reviewing the results in which that danger was embodied, went as follows: 1- It created a large sector of Muslim intellectuals convinced that Islam is not suitable for building an educational system that meets the requirements of the age. 2- Accompanied by the treatment of Islam by intellectuals as religion is treated in the Western system—religious education in public schools—as merely a school subject. 3- It caused indifference among Muslims regarding the development and modernization of the traditional Islamic system, thereby confirming the colonizer's accusation that Islam is not suitable—originally—for development and modernization. 4- It isolated Islamic scholars from leadership positions—accordingly—intellectually, socially, and politically, and replaced them with secular leaderships in their education and thus their reference. It was able to put forward the idea of equality of cultures, which allowed the idea of nationalism to be presented as an alternative to Islam, so nationalist leaderships came and seized the reins of new institutions, at the expense of the absence of the Muslim intellectual. On the other hand, the danger of this duality is manifested in that it does not stop its separation (religious from secular) at the limit of external structure only, but goes beyond that to include the entire curriculum and its objectives, and thus the natural outcome of this clear imbalance becomes the existence of two types of personality.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion on the unity of knowledge in Islamic education and the dangers of a religious-secular duality. The author begins by stating that all fields of knowledge are a single unit in Islamic educational philosophy, emanating from a holistic worldview. There is no distinction between cosmic sciences (like natural sciences) and religious sciences in terms of their origin and method. This unity is objective because the Creator, man, and the universe are one. The author then addresses the concept of specialization, acknowledging its practical necessity due to the expansion of knowledge, but emphasizing that unity must not be forgotten. Historical examples of specialists like Hunayn ibn Ishaq, Ibn Sina, and al-Kindi are cited to show that specialization existed within the framework of knowledge unity. The author then identifies the real danger: imagining a dualistic split between religious and secular education. This dualism, according to the author, has led to several negative consequences: it convinced many Muslim intellectuals that Islam cannot build a modern educational system; it reduced Islam to a mere school subject; it caused indifference to the development of the traditional system; it isolated Islamic scholars and replaced them with secular leaders; and it promoted nationalism over Islam. The passage ends by noting that this duality affects not just the external structure but the entire curriculum and objectives, resulting in a split personality. The author is arguing for the preservation of the unity of knowledge as a foundational principle in Islamic education.

Key Terms
وحدة المعرفة
ثنائية
تكامل المعرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the unity of all fields of knowledge in Islamic education?
A) The need for specialization in the modern age
B) The holistic Islamic worldview that sees a single origin and purpose for all knowledge
C) The historical existence of encyclopedic scholars
D) The separation of religious and secular sciences

Key Takeaway
Islamic education must preserve the fundamental unity of knowledge while accommodating practical specialization.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the author's reasoning, write a brief paragraph explaining why the study of physics should be considered part of Islamic education, not separate from it.
?
Reflect on your own educational background: are there any signs of the duality the author warns against? How could the principle of unity of knowledge be applied to create a more integrated curriculum?

intermediate
8 min
The Danger of Duality (Thuna'iyya)
Author outlines the dangers of a religious-secular educational duality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the negative consequences of the religious-secular duality in education as described by the author.

Core Idea
A split between religious and secular education leads to intellectual confusion, marginalization of scholars, and societal fragmentation.

The author warns that beyond the practical need for specialization, a conceptual duality between religious and secular education is a real danger. He enumerates five consequences from a researcher's analysis, showing how this duality undermines Islamic identity, isolates scholars, and promotes secular nationalism. Understanding these consequences helps us recognize warning signs in contemporary educational systems.

Guided Path
1
Define the duality at issue
The author specifies the duality (thuna'iyya) as a split between religious education (al-ta'lim al-dini) and secular education (al-ta'lim al-madani). It is not just a division of subjects but a conceptual separation that treats them as incompatible.
Contrast this with the earlier acceptance of specialization within unity.
2
List the five consequences
Find the numbered list in the passage. The author presents five outcomes: (1) Muslim intellectuals doubt Islam's suitability for modern education; (2) Islam is treated as a mere school subject; (3) Muslims become indifferent to developing traditional Islamic education; (4) Islamic scholars are isolated from leadership and replaced by secular leaders; (5) the idea of equality of cultures promotes nationalism over Islam.
The consequences are cumulative; each reinforces the next.
3
Analyze the logical progression
Notice how the consequences build: first, a loss of confidence in Islam's relevance, then a reduction of Islam to a subject, then indifference, then marginalization of scholars, and finally a shift from Islamic identity to nationalism. This shows how duality erodes the foundations of Islamic society.
4
Recognize the depth of the danger
The author emphasizes that the duality does not stop at the external structure (building) of schools but penetrates the curriculum and objectives, resulting in a 'split personality' (naghin min al-shakhsiyya). This means the duality affects individuals' identity and worldview.
The phrase 'two types of personality' indicates the psychological and cultural damage.

All fields of knowledge are one unit in the view of Islamic education; there is no difference between cosmic sciences and religious sciences in terms of knowledge and method in research and thinking, because their source is one, the Creator is one, man is one, and the universe is one. Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion on the unity of knowledge in Islamic education and the dangers of a religious-secular duality. Which of the following is NOT one of the consequences of the religious-secular duality listed in the passage?
A) Muslim intellectuals become convinced that Islam cannot build a modern educational system.

?
List the five negative consequences of duality given in the passage. For each one, write a one-sentence countermeasure that a unified educational system could implement to avoid that consequence.
?
Identify an example of the duality from your own context (e.g., a curriculum that treats 'Islamic studies' as a separate subject unrelated to science). Write a short proposal for integrating the subject with science teaching, based on the unity principle.

beginner
5 min
Identifying Epistemological Dualism in Islamic Education
Author analyzes dualism's harmful effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key characteristics of dualism between religious and secular education and analyze its consequences as argued in the passage.

Core Idea
Dualism splits knowledge and personality, undermining the Islamic unity of creed and culture.

The passage warns against the danger of separating religious (dīnī) and secular (madani) education. This dualism, the author argues, is not just an administrative arrangement but a fundamental epistemological split that produces two conflicting worldviews and personality types. Understanding this critique equips you to recognize similar dualistic assumptions in contemporary Muslim discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two poles of dualism
What are the two types of education being separated? Search the Arabic for 'تعليم ديني' and 'تعليم مدني' — religious vs. secular/civil education.
The passage explicitly names these as the two poles of the dualism.
2
Extract the five consequences listed by the researcher
The author cites a researcher who lists five results. List them in order: 1) Muslim intellectuals doubt Islam's suitability, 2) Islam treated as a mere subject, 3) indifference to traditional system development, 4) isolation of scholars, 5) promotion of nationalism as alternative.
These are enumerated with hyphens in the Arabic.
3
Analyze the deeper effect on personality
The passage says the imbalance produces two personality types: one from Islamic education (faith, piety) and one from secular education (self-sufficiency). How do these conflict?
The secular type is described as thinking it can do without God's guidance.
4
Examine the failure of traditional scholars
What does the author say about the response of Muslim scholars? They confronted dualism but neglected to confront imported secular ideas, preserving spirituality only in a limited sector.
This led to cultural duality between religious scholars and secularists.
5
Synthesize the overall epistemological danger
Why does this dualism threaten the unity of knowledge and identity? The passage concludes that inconsistency between creed and curricula deprives the system of legitimacy.
The Mecca conference called it 'nearly impossible' to reconcile the two concepts of personality.

٤ - عَزَلَ علماء الإسلام عن المواقع القيادية - تبعا لذلك – فكريًا واجتماعيا وسياسيا، واستبدلهم بقيادات علمانية في تعليمها ومن ثم مرجعيتها.
استطاع أن يطرح فكرة تكافؤ الثقافات، مما أتاح طرح فكرة القومية بديلا عن الإسلام، فأتت قيادات قومية أمسكت بزمام المؤسسات الجديدة، على حساب غياب المثقف المسلم).
ومن جانب آخر يتجلى خطر هذه الثنائية في كونها لا تقف بفصلها (الديني عن المدني عند حد البناء الخارجي فحسب، بل تتعدى ذلك لتشمل جملة المنهاج وأهدافه، وبذلك تصبح المحصلة الطبيعية لهذا الخلل الواضح وجود نغطين من الشخصية
أحدهما نتاج نظام تعليم إسلامي ملؤه الإيمان والورع والتقوى. ثانيهما: نتاج أو مخرج نظام تعليم علماني يظن أنه وحده قادر على صنع كل شيء بلا حدود لطاقته ولا حاجة لهداية الله وتوفيقه.
ولذلك فقد خرج المؤتمرون في المؤتمر الأول للتعليم الإسلامي المنعقد بمكة المكرمة بأنه من شبه المستحيل التوفيق بين مفهومين متناقضين عن الشخصية الإنسانية، حيث هي في الإسلام جوانب متكاملة من الروح والأخلاق وأي نشاط إنساني آخر فرديًا كان أم جماعياً في حين أن طرق التدريس الغربية تقوم بتنحية الجانب الروحي للإنسان.
إن عدم الانسجام بين عقيدة الأمة وثقافتها من جهة وبين المناهج بجميع عناصرها من أهداف ومحتوى ووسائل وأنشطة مختلفة وتقويم من جهة أخرى يمثل سببًا رئيسا في بروز مشكلة الانفصام النكد في النظام المعرفي التعليمي في العالم الإسلامي، مما أفقده الشرعية.
وقبالة ذلك الوضع بدأت مجابهة علماء المسلمين – الذين تلقوا تعليـمـا إسلاميا تقليدياً - لفكرة الثنائية، ولكنهم أغفلوا مواجهة الأفكار والمفهومات العلمانية المستوردة، فتمكنوا من الإبقاء على المفهومات الروحية في قطاع محدود قطاعات المجتمع، مما أدى إلى ظهور الازدواجية الثقافية في العالم الإسلامي، بين طبقة علماء الدين أو التعليم الإسلامي، وبين نظام التعليم الحديث الذي أدى إلى خلق طبقة العلمانيين.
Chapter Two: First Section - Ethics of Knowledge and Its Unity
Therefore there is no problem from this perspective, but the real danger lies in imagining the outbreak of a dualism that separates its two poles such as the dualism of religious education and secular education.
One researcher goes through the results in which that danger was embodied as follows:
-1- It created a large sector of Muslim intellectuals who are convinced that Islam is not suitable for building an educational system that suits the requirements of the age.
2 - This was accompanied by the intellectuals treating Islam as religion is treated in the Western system of religious education in public schools, as merely a school subject.
It caused indifference among Muslims regarding the issue of developing and modernizing the traditional Islamic system, which confirmed the colonizer's accusation that Islam is not suitable - fundamentally - for development and modernization.
4 - It isolated Islamic scholars from leadership positions - accordingly - intellectually, socially, and politically, and replaced them with secular leaderships in their education and consequently their reference.
It was able to promote the idea of equivalence of cultures, which allowed the idea of nationalism to be presented as an alternative to Islam, so nationalist leaderships came and took control of the new institutions, at the expense of the absence of the Muslim intellectual.
On the other hand, the danger of this dualism manifests in that it does not stop at separating the religious from the secular at the level of external structure only, but extends to include the entire curriculum and its objectives, and thus the natural outcome of this clear imbalance is the existence of two types of personality:
One is the product of an Islamic educational system full of faith, piety, and reverence. The second is the product or output of a secular educational system that thinks it alone is capable of making everything without limits to its capacity and without need for God's guidance and success.
Therefore, the participants in the first Islamic education conference held in Mecca concluded that it is nearly impossible to reconcile two contradictory concepts of human personality, where it is in Islam integrated aspects of spirit, ethics, and any other human activity whether individual or collective, while Western teaching methods set aside the spiritual aspect of man.
The inconsistency between the creed and culture of the nation on one hand and the curricula with all their elements of objectives, content, means, various activities, and evaluation on the other hand represents a major cause for the emergence of the bitter problem of schizophrenia in the cognitive educational system in the Islamic world, which deprived it of legitimacy.
Facing that situation, Muslim scholars who received traditional Islamic education began to confront the idea of dualism, but they neglected to confront the imported secular ideas and concepts, so they were able to preserve spiritual concepts in a limited sector of society's sectors, leading to the emergence of cultural duality in the Islamic world between the class of religious scholars or Islamic education and the modern education system that led to the creation of the secularist class.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological critique of the dualism between religious and secular education in the Muslim world. The author begins by stating that the real danger is not from external problems but from the imagined separation (thunā'iyya) between the two poles of religious (dīnī) and secular (madani) education. Then a researcher is cited listing several harmful consequences: first, it created a large group of Muslim intellectuals who doubt Islam's suitability for modern education. Second, these intellectuals treat Islam as merely a school subject like in Western secular systems. Third, it caused indifference to traditional Islamic system development, reinforcing colonial accusations. Fourth, it isolated Islamic scholars from leadership and replaced them with secular elites. Fifth, it promoted cultural equivalence and nationalism as alternatives to Islam. The author adds that this dualism extends beyond external structure to the entire curriculum and objectives, resulting in two conflicting personality types: one religious and pious, the other secular and self-sufficient. The conclusion of the first Islamic education conference in Mecca is cited: it is nearly impossible to reconcile the integrated Islamic concept of human personality with the Western approach that neglects the spiritual. Finally, the author notes that Muslim scholars who confronted dualism failed to address imported secular ideas, leading to a cultural duality between religious scholars and the secular educated class. The passage uses a critical tone to argue that epistemological dualism undermines the unity of knowledge and identity.

Key Terms
ثنائية
تعليم ديني
تعليم مدني
انفصام
ازدواجية ثقافية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one consequence of the dualism between religious and secular education?
A) It leads to improved integration of knowledge.
B) It creates a large sector of Muslim intellectuals who doubt Islam's suitability for modern education.
C) It strengthens the role of Islamic scholars in leadership positions.
D) It encourages the development of a unified educational curriculum.

Key Takeaway
The dualism between religious and secular education creates a split in knowledge and personality, leading to the marginalization of Islamic values in modern educational systems.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: According to the passage, list the five consequences of educational dualism as presented by the researcher. For each consequence, explain in one sentence how it undermines Islamic education.
?
Task 2: Compare the two personality types described in the passage. Identify which characteristics correspond to each type and argue whether the passage's description of the secular type as 'self-sufficient' is fair.
